Current Affairs Commentary

Another Test of the Non-Recognition Doctrine 19

When the puppet state was first established, Xie Jieshi once issued a public announcement to foreign countries, using the opening of the Manchurian door and the fulfillment of international obligations as bait to entice countries to grant it formal recognition. However, all countries, adhering to the spirit of the League of Nations resolutions and the Stimson Doctrine, generally ignored it. The Japanese, although outwardly calm about this international non-recognition doctrine and feigning indifference, actually felt it like a bone stuck in their throat, unable to be removed. Ultimately, they colluded with the small Central American country of El Salvador, hoping to salvage something from the situation. Their painstaking efforts were both pitiful and frightening.

The Japanese, on the one hand, wanted to gain a glimmer of international sympathy, and on the other hand, wanted to ensure the overall control of the puppet Manchuria, which led to contradictions between their words and deeds, and they were unable to resolve the situation themselves. From the establishment of the puppet Manchuria until today, foreigners in Manchuria still enjoy consular jurisdiction, and consuls of countries other than Japan stationed in Manchuria still perform their duties based on the "recognition certificates" issued by the Chairman of the Chinese National Government. At the same time, they continue to be under the control of their embassies in China. These two points are sufficient to demonstrate that the so-called non-recognition doctrine has its positive significance. The reason why Japan and the puppet Manchuria authorities have tacitly acquiesced in the past is that the overall situation was not yet settled, and they did not want to act too hastily.

However, the Japanese are ultimately unwilling to simply ignore this expedient measure. Moreover, with the increasingly tense relations between Japan and Russia and the upcoming London Conference, the uncertain international status of the puppet Manchuria will pose a major hidden danger for the future. Once Japan and Russia go to war, the puppet Manchuria is bound by the "Japan-Manchuria Protocol" and cannot but take the same position as Japan and participate in the war. However, in the eyes of neutral countries, the puppet Manchuria is still Chinese territory. If China does not participate in the war, how can the puppet Manchuria act on its own? If the puppet Manchuria declares itself a belligerent, it will inevitably have the determination to implement international law during wartime. The resulting disputes will be serious. We all know that in the Second Russo-Japanese War, the Japanese will exert the power of their superior navy. However, due to the limitations of naval treaties, they cannot expand it as much as they would like, so they have to borrow the name of the puppet Manchuria navy to build warships. It is expected that during the future Russo-Japanese War, Japanese warships flying the puppet Manchuria flag will appear on the high seas to exercise the right to search neutral ships. However, if neutral countries do not first recognize the puppet Manchuria as a state, not only will it be unable to fulfill its wartime mission, but it will also cause major conflicts with neutral countries and put Japan in a difficult position. Even the interests of foreigners within the puppet Manchuria will be affected by the distinction between the belligerent and neutral status of the local area. If this is not resolved, there will inevitably be many disputes. It can be asserted. Moreover, the Japanese are confident of victory in the war against Russia. According to their prediction, Korea at the end of the First Russo-Japanese War is equivalent to today's puppet Manchuria. The puppet Manchuria at the end of the Second Russo-Japanese War will be like Korea today. If the puppet Manchuria can gain the recognition of various countries as soon as possible, it can merge with Japan at that time and directly copy the story of the annexation of Korea without seeking the understanding of various countries again.

Furthermore, although Japan is building warships by borrowing the name of the puppet Manchuria, it cannot do as it pleases due to the monitoring of countries such as the United Kingdom and the United States. If the puppet Manchuria can be recognized by various countries and join the international community, then expanding its navy at any time would be its inherent right, and other countries would not be able to interfere. If that were the case, the Japanese could have already secured victory without waiting for the negotiations at the London Conference.

However, the powers have long understood the Japanese mentality, and the non-recognition doctrine is perhaps even more in the actual interests of countries such as the United Kingdom, the United States, and Russia than it is in China. Therefore, even without the constraints of the League of Nations resolutions and the Stimson Declaration, they would certainly not abandon it rashly. According to a Reuters dispatch from Tokyo on the 19th, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs intends to revise the principle of equal opportunity for opening the Manchurian door as a prelude to forced recognition. Recently, the Kwantung Army Headquarters has also demanded the prohibition of the movement of British troops within the Shanhaiguan area, causing embarrassment to the countries that signed the Boxer Protocol. Their intention is nothing more than to make various countries feel the practical difficulties. Even if they cannot actively recognize "Manchukuo" as an independent country, they should at least tacitly acknowledge "Manchukuo" as not being Chinese territory. It is still difficult to predict how these two matters will change. However, the non-recognition doctrine will face another serious test, which is beyond doubt. Will countries other than the United Kingdom, the United States, and Russia be able to maintain their original position, or will they succumb to Japanese threats?

Soviet Russia Uncovers Major Espionage Case, Korean Leader Sentenced to Death by Firing Squad 24

The Remaining Twenty-Three Sentenced to Imprisonment

Allegedly Plotted to Sabotage Russian Rear During Wartime

(Moscow) During the Soviet Russian Supreme Court Military Collegium's trial of arrested spies, the activities of a major espionage organization were uncovered, with particular emphasis on the Soviet Russian Far Eastern Railway transportation. The leader of the organization was Korean Kim Jae-won (transliteration). It was heard that his party members had received special training in tasks such as destroying roads, preparing to hinder the Russian army's rear during wartime. It was also heard that the organization had secured responsible positions for its members in the railway, so its sabotage work sometimes resulted in deaths and injuries to many people. All twenty-three of those being interrogated were sentenced. Their leader, Kim Jae-won, and others have been sentenced to death by firing squad today. The rest were sentenced to imprisonment for up to ten years. (Reuters dispatch on the 23rd)

(Moscow) The Military Collegium of the Supreme Court of the USSR, under the direction of Uliech, has completed its trial of a spy and sabotage ring operating in several parts of the Soviet railway system.

During the trial, it was revealed that the mission of the ring was to collect information on railway carrying capacity and mobilization preparations (especially regarding railways connecting central USSR and the Far East) as well as the condition of locomotive repairs throughout the Soviet Union (especially the main lines in the Far East). At the same time, they conducted sabotage work on the railway and in locomotive repair shops and made various preparations for large-scale sabotage work in the event of war.

The organization included Soviet state employees who betrayed the interests of their country, including officials of the central apparatus of the Transport Commission and officials of its local apparatus. The leader of the ring was an espionage and sabotage agent, Kim Ruoyin (transliteration), a Korean from Manchuria and an agent of a foreign secret organization. These traitors received rewards from Kim, conducted large-scale reconnaissance activities, collected secret materials, and sought to damage vehicles, destroy railway factories, and damage machinery in locomotive repair shops, in order to carry out various sabotage activities on the railway. These acts of sabotage include the train wreck at the Zhuo'erna'ye station on the Moscow-Kazan railway, where two locomotives derailed, fifteen trains were destroyed, and many people were killed and injured, resulting in the interruption of traffic on the main line. Other incidents include the collision of two freight trains at Panji station and the destruction of a suburban passenger train outside Udel'naya station. The machinery and lathes of the Molom locomotive repair shop were systematically damaged under the instructions of Yalamashantrovski and Sveridov. In short, these traitors who betrayed their country have caused significant damage to Soviet railway transportation.

A total of twenty-three people were interrogated by the Military Collegium. Considering that the personnel of this spy and sabotage group were engaged in destroying one of the most important sectors of the national economy, namely railway transportation, and that all members of the group were Soviet employees, they committed a direct crime against the motherland. In addition, all leaders and organizers of espionage and sabotage activities, as well as the most active spies, must be subjected to the death penalty. Therefore, the leader of the ring, the Korean Kim Ruoyin, and his closest aides, namely Slasedning, an expert in the locomotive department of the Transport Commission, Aleksandrov, Koshlov, Mishin, and Sveridov, the director of the technical department of the Molom locomotive repair shop, Porovski, the stationmaster of the Moscow-Pasachi'erskaya station on the Moscow-Kazan railway, and the locomotive engineer Mozhainov, were sentenced to death by firing squad for being the organizers of espionage and sabotage activities and the most active spies and saboteurs.

Other defendants, including Rodonov, an expert in the locomotive department of the Transport Commission, Seredenski, the chief of the first section of the Moscow-Kazan railway, and other individuals, were sentenced to imprisonment for ten years or less. (TASS dispatch on the 24th)

US and Japan Only an Arrow's Flight Apart in Alaska, a Crucial Military Location 25

US Plans to Establish New Naval Base

To Create Grounds for Dealing with Japan's Demand for Equality

(Washington) Several of the new naval bases that the United States plans to establish in the Pacific are, in terms of flight speed, only an arrow's flight away from the Japanese coast. The United States may use them to deal with Japan's demand for naval equality. The Associated Press learned today from reliable sources that someone has informally proposed this plan to the US government in preparation for dealing with Japan's demand for equality. One of the proposed bases is Dutch Harbor in Alaska, only 700 miles from the Asian continent. It is remembered that during the Washington Conference, the United States promised to abandon all naval bases in the Pacific in order to induce Japan to accept the 5:5:3 naval ratio. Therefore, observers believe that if Japan insists on demanding equality, then the United States resuming the establishment of naval bases is also within expectations. They believe that the Navy's dispatch of aircraft and submarines to Dutch Harbor in Alaska, the Army's aircraft flying to Alaska, and the US fleet's planned naval exercises in Alaska next year are all signs of a storm brewing. (National Telegram on the 23rd)

US Aircraft Flies Over Dangerous Section En Route to Alaska 26

Juneau, Alaska Peninsula. Ten US Army bomber aircraft flying from the United States landed at Whitehorse, Yukon, at 6:55 PM yesterday (local time). The aircraft's route involved flying over the Canadian Rocky Mountains, which was one of the most difficult sections, and it has now been successfully completed. It is said that this flight by the US Army aircraft squadron is quite important. Former Army Aviation Commander Mitchell once said that if the United States uses Alaska as an air force base, it will be able to control the whole world. (Havas dispatch on the 24th)

Contents of the US Air Defense Investigation Report 27

(New York) The special committee established by the US Department of War to investigate the US aviation industry released its investigation report today. The report contains some corrections to the theory of sky attacks.

Enemy Aircraft Have No Offensive Capabilities. The report states that there is no need to worry about an attack on the United States from the sky at present, as there are currently no aircraft capable of flying across the Pacific or Atlantic Ocean to attack important central locations in the United States. If an enemy air force wants to attack the United States, it must use warships in the ocean as its base, and these warships must be in locations where the US fleet cannot attack them. Otherwise, it must have the support of the army, and this army must be stationed on or near US territory. For example, last year, Italian Air Minister Balbo's aircraft squadron flew across the Atlantic Ocean to the United States, stopping in eight locations on foreign territory and eleven locations on ocean warships. The preparation period, from the beginning of preparation to the arrival at the destination, lasted a total of thirty-three days.

Establish Base in Alaska. The report advocates that the United States must maintain sufficient air bases, at least one air base must be established in Alaska, as that area is vulnerable to attacks by the Japanese Navy and Air Force. The Aleutian Islands are Militarily Important. Some people believe that if the Aleutian Islands in the Pacific are properly organized, they can be used as a base for effective attacks against Japan.

Lijun's Message to Quangu 28

I arrived in Shanghai yesterday with my parents to visit your residence but was disappointed to find that you had moved and I could not see you. Please send a letter as soon as possible to Shanghai Post Office Box 1667, as I will be returning to the Philippines in two months. Opposes Merging the Army, Navy, and Air Force. In addition, the US Air Force has always been divided into the Army Air Corps and the Navy Air Corps. Some people have advocated merging them under unified command. The report opposes this proposal, stating that the current Japanese Air Force is also separately commanded by the Army and Navy, which is the same as in the United States.

Suggests Encouraging Private Industry. In addition, the report suggests encouraging commercially run aircraft industries and that state-owned aircraft manufacturing plants should not compete with private factories. Efforts should be made to facilitate the export of aviation equipment, as the reason why US aircraft manufacturing is superior to other countries is that the US aircraft industry is not subject to the control of military agencies.

Purchase More Aircraft and Train Personnel. The report advocates that the government purchase a large number of aircraft and increase funding for training aircraft pilots. The report argues that the United States should have a total of 2,320 aircraft and a corresponding number of pilots. When necessary, aviation personnel should be eliminated and replaced with younger elements. All Army officers should receive thorough aviation training. The report also states that Colonel Lindbergh advocates developing the use of aircraft engines, increasing it from 1,500 horsepower to 2,000 horsepower. (Havas dispatch on the 23rd)

No Mention of Large Airship Policy. (Washington) The Army Air Corps investigation report of the Joint Military and Civilian Committee was submitted to Secretary of War Dunn yesterday by the chairman of the committee, Pei Kaier. It completely fails to mention the much-disputed issue of large airships, only suggesting that the military continue to test the use of these airships for reconnaissance and other military purposes. The committee has a total of eleven members, six representatives of the people and five military personnel. They generally agreed with the report that the Army Air Corps lagged behind the US Navy and commercial aviation. Du Lie'er, a famous high-speed aviator who was originally a member of the Army Air Corps, added a separate report, strongly advocating that the Air Corps should be separated from the General Staff Headquarters. The general report refers to the idea of merging the air forces of the Army and Navy and establishing a separate aviation department as an extravagant waste that cannot be implemented. (National Telegram on the 23rd)

Roosevelt's Itinerary for Tour of Honolulu 29

Will Inspect Defense Forces Tomorrow, Will Depart for US at the End of the Week

USS Houston. The USS Houston, carrying President Roosevelt, was visible off the coast of the Hawaiian Islands this morning. Parliament Building Noises Overhead, British House of Lords Passes Air Force Bill, Secretary of State for Air Speaks in Defense 30

The British Air Force Should Be Equal in Strength to That Across the Channel

Policy Perspective Aims at Peace, Not Aggression

(London) Since Acting Prime Minister Baldwin presented the British plan to increase air force armaments over five years in the House of Commons last Friday, the question of expanding the air force has become the main goal of debate in the House of Commons. The Labor opposition members of the House of Commons have already proposed a motion, stating that it is regrettable that the British cabinet has decided to increase armaments after discussions between Britain and France have just concluded at the disarmament conference. Therefore, this afternoon, Secretary of State for Air, Londonderry, attended the House of Lords to deliver a speech defending the government's five-year air force plan and answering the opposition's questions in the House of Commons. The speech stated briefly: During the Great War, Britain was the world's largest air power, but today it has fallen to fifth place. In 1923, Britain had already established a plan to build 52 squadrons of aircraft, but this plan was delayed due to disarmament negotiations. The government's announced plan to build an air force in 1934 and the four years thereafter is actually just a revival of old matters, in an attempt to remedy Britain's unbearable weakness. Any responsible government that knows it should use all means and all power to seek national security will not allow our country's air force to remain in a small and weak position for long. The government deeply understands that appropriate air defense is necessary for the empire's safety, and therefore, it has decided that the British air force should be on par with the largest air force capable of attacking the British coast. This is the main policy of our national defense. We seek equality in the air force, and there are four ways to achieve this: First, completely abolish naval and army military aircraft. At the same time, we must find ways to ensure that civil aircraft are not used for military purposes. If so, the air forces of all countries will be equal to zero, with no distinction in strength. Second, other countries take the lead in reducing their air forces to be equal to our British level. In other words, all countries reduce their air force strength to the extent agreed upon by all countries. Third, Britain builds an air force to be equal in strength to the largest air force capable of attacking the British coast. Fourth, the second and third methods are implemented simultaneously. On the one hand, countries jointly seek to reduce their air forces, and on the other hand, Britain builds an air force to seek equality. From this perspective, our views are clear and practical. Our country must have an air force that is as strong as the air force of any country capable of attacking the British coast. If so, our power to strive for peace can be enhanced, and it will not be a small contribution to the suppression of the arms race. Britain has always hoped to establish an international agreement to limit air forces, just as it hopes to limit all armaments. However, the air force policy that Britain is now adopting will be able to promote the early establishment of an agreement to limit air forces. This is what I earnestly hope for. Last November, I made a statement to you on this issue. You should still remember that at that time, I said that like a balance scale, one end is the plate of aggression, and the other end is the plate of peace. All of Britain's national power, like a weight, is placed in the plate of peace policy, which is beyond doubt. However, if we now argue that the weight of Britain's sword does not have to exceed the weight of the aggression side, then there is nothing more encouraging to the policy of aggression than this, etc. After Londonderry finished his speech, Labor opposition member Lord Ponsonby was about to stand up to reply when suddenly a loud noise was heard from the roof, and a fighter plane was soaring over the parliament building. It turned out that Britain was conducting air defense exercises from today until Friday, with the aim of determining whether, if foreign aircraft attacked from the south, they could cause damage to London. After a while, Ponsonby spoke, first saying that the government's proposed policy of air force equality would actually lead to an air force arms race among countries, and that the Secretary of State for Air had just finished his speech when a fighter plane flew over the parliament building roof, which was such a coincidence, what else could this be but an omen. Finally, he said that the Labor Party supports the Geneva policy and advocates joint action by all countries to safeguard peace and punish aggressors, and that this position will never change. After Ponsonby finished his speech, the House of Lords held a vote, and the government's air force policy was passed by a large majority of 54 votes to 9. (Havas Telegram, 23rd)

(London) According to Secretary of State for Air Lord Londonderry, who told the House of Lords today, the procedure for Britain to expand its air force will cost a total of 20 million pounds by 1938. This procedure aims to reverse the arms race. In the future, when it is completed, the position of the Royal Air Force will not reach equality unless Britain continues to build, and it will be easy to continue the expansion and achieve rapid success. However, he hopes that this situation can be avoided through international agreements. According to the Secretary of State for Air's remarks, this was in response to Labor MP Lord Ponsonby's motion expressing regret over the increase in armaments before the end of the disarmament conference. (Reuters Telegram, 23rd)

London Air Defense Drill 31

Searchlights Illuminate the Dark Night, More Than 300 Aircraft Participate

(London) Last night, aircraft circled over London and searchlights flashed. The British Air Force held a military exercise, with 200 bombers attacking London. This aerial exercise will continue until Friday. Its purpose is to test the efficiency of the British Air Force. The Air Force is divided into two teams: the attackers are the Northern Army and the defenders are the Southern Army. The Southern Army has 180 aircraft, all of which are fighters and reconnaissance aircraft, assisted by searchlight teams. The attacking army began its attack last night, with the sound of engines rumbling all night. They competed to drop bombs on London. The defenders used 150 searchlights to detect the location of the attacking army and intercepted them with fighter aircraft. According to the opinions of those in London who are paying attention to this matter, many of the attacking aircraft penetrated the defense line and dropped bombs on their targets. However, the referees have not yet announced their decision. (Reuters Telegram, 24th)

Belgium Joins the Kellogg-Briand Pact 34

(Geneva) The "General Treaty for Renunciation of War as an Instrument of National Policy" (referred to as the "Kellogg-Briand Pact"), which was initiated by former French Foreign Minister Briand and U.S. Secretary of State Kellogg and signed in Paris on August 27, 1928, has been signed and ratified by the majority of countries. However, Belgium has not yet joined. Today, the French government notified the Secretariat of the League of Nations that the Belgian government had notified the U.S. government, declaring that Belgium would join the Kellogg-Briand Pact. U.S.-Russian Debt Negotiations 39

Negotiations to Be Held in Washington Today

(Washington) Secretary of State Hull announced today that negotiations on Soviet Russia's debt to the U.S. will begin on Wednesday at the State Department. Both diplomatic and financial circles are paying close attention to this announcement, saying that discussions may eliminate a layer of obstacles to U.S.-Russian trade. Because the Department of Justice has listed Soviet Russia as a debtor nation under the Johnson Act, it cannot raise new debts in the U.S. again. The debt being discussed this time totals US$768,500,000, which is the debt issued during the Tsarist and Kerensky governments and not recognized by the Worker-Peasant Government. In addition, there is also the property of American people that was confiscated by the Soviet Russian government when it nationalized all property, valued at US$440,000,000. For 16 years, the U.S. government has insisted that this loss must be compensated before recognizing Soviet Russia. Even at the time of recognition last year, it was stipulated that negotiations must be conducted to resolve the issue. Russia believes that this debt was borrowed by the previous government to oppress the people, so it refuses to pay it. Later, Russia also demanded compensation for the occupation of Siberia and other places by the Allied forces, and was willing to convert the old debt into new debt, so the prospect of negotiations appeared. Although the amount demanded by Soviet Russia from the U.S. has not been mentioned, it was initially claimed that the total amount demanded from various countries reached a huge US$600 million. Now that other countries have repeatedly found solutions with Soviet Russia, the U.S. should also be able to use indirect compensation methods as the basis for discussion. (National Telegram, 23rd)

America Eliminates a Major Scourge, Entire Nation Celebrates 53

Chicago: The killing of the notorious American bandit Dillinger is cause for celebration throughout the nation, and especially among the people of the Midwest who have suffered at his hands. London Copper Prices Plunge 54

(London) Copper prices plummeted today. While surplus metal reserves had decreased slightly in the first half of the year, metal prices remained weak. Now, copper prices have fallen sharply again. This is partly due to the poor situation in Germany, which has reduced its raw material imports to the lowest possible level. As a result, American metal merchants are dumping their surplus production on the London market at reduced prices. Furthermore, the mines in the Belgian Congo in Central Africa are becoming serious competitors. They can still make a profit even selling at the current low prices. Their aim is to sell goods, with maintaining prices as a secondary concern. Unless American commerce revives in the autumn, easing the pressure of American copper in London, and European purchasing power increases slightly, the current situation is unlikely to improve. (Reuters, 24th)

Development of Japanese-Dutch Commercial Conference (Batavia Correspondence) 98

Disputes arise over exchanged goods

Third meeting has a breakthrough

Decision made to form a separate expert committee for discussion

Since Japan, with its low labor costs and convenient transportation, implemented a policy of dumping in Southeast Asia, the market in the Dutch East Indies has been almost entirely monopolized. Not only has the sales of goods from European countries been greatly affected, but the market for products from the Netherlands itself is also in danger of being completely seized, posing a great threat to agriculture and industry in the Dutch East Indies. For example, Java has had abundant harvests for many years, with ample food supply. If the import of cheap Japanese rice is allowed to continue freely, local rice prices will inevitably plummet, severely impacting the livelihood of farmers. If the indigenous people take actions beyond the law due to their inability to maintain their lives, the impact on public order will be significant. Therefore, in order to maintain public order and protect local agricultural products, the Dutch East Indies government had no choice but to promulgate regulations restricting the import of foreign rice. Similarly, cheap Japanese cement almost defeated cement from Padang. To protect its own industry, the Dutch East Indies also had to restrict the import of Japanese goods. Furthermore, the "sarong" (a type of skirt worn by indigenous men and women) industry was originally the most important indigenous industry in the Dutch East Indies, but due to the dumping of Japanese goods over the years, the sarong industry of the indigenous people has been greatly affected, almost to the point of complete bankruptcy. Moreover, the "sarongs" imported from the Netherlands have also been gradually decreasing due to the exclusion of Japanese goods. If this is not remedied soon, sales will inevitably be completely blocked. Therefore, in order to protect indigenous industry and promote the sales of products from the Netherlands, regulations restricting the import of textiles could not but be promulgated.

After the Dutch East Indies successively promulgated various restrictive regulations, Japan was greatly alarmed, as it realized that the hard-won good market would soon be lost as a result. Therefore, it had no choice but to find ways to salvage the situation, and proposed to the Netherlands to open a "Japanese-Dutch Commercial Conference," hoping to imitate the precedent of the Japanese-Indian conference, and use the method of dividing the Indian market with Britain to divide the East Indian market with the Netherlands. However, the Japanese-Indian agreement was able to be established because Indian cotton was needed by Japan, and textiles were also needed by India. Therefore, both sides were happy to accept the exchange of cotton for textiles. But the situation in the Dutch East Indies was different, as it had no goods that Japan needed. The Dutch East Indies' largest exports were sugar, tin, copra, rubber, tobacco, coffee, and kerosene. Among them, the sales of sugar were the worst. If Japan wanted to reach an agreement with the Dutch East Indies to exchange goods, the Dutch East Indies was very willing to exchange sugar for Japanese goods. However, Japan absolutely did not need sugar from the Dutch East Indies, because sugar from Taiwan was not only sufficient for Japan's use, but it was also planning to expand into the world market. Therefore, Japan only wanted to buy more of the Dutch East Indies' rubber, tobacco, coffee, and kerosene. The Dutch East Indies insisted that sugar must be exchanged. Disputes arose between the two sides as a result.

The Japanese-Dutch conference was originally scheduled to be held in May, but it did not begin until the end of June. As of the 27th of last month, representatives from both sides had held three meetings. During the first and second meetings, the representatives from both sides held their own views, resulting in nothing but heated debates. Japan's reason was that the recent actions of the Dutch East Indies, restricting the import of Japanese goods, violated the "most favored nation" clause in the "Japanese-Dutch Treaty of Commerce and Navigation," and its attitude was very strong. The Dutch side's attitude was also very strong, stating that "in view of the fierce competition of Japanese goods in the Dutch East Indies market, the Dutch East Indies government, in order to stabilize the economic and social life of the country and to prevent abnormal disturbances in the economic situation of the Dutch East Indies, had to adopt this new measure based on the country's absolute freedom of action." With both sides insisting on their own positions, it was extremely difficult to be optimistic about the future. However, during the third meeting on June 27, the two sides suddenly decided to organize an expert committee to invite experts to collect various reports and then conduct detailed discussions. Although it is still difficult to predict the outcome of the discussions at this time, it cannot be said that this move is not a major turning point in the overall situation. From the reporter's observation, it is expected that the Dutch side will inevitably make considerable concessions in the end, as it is difficult to achieve the goal of insisting on exchanging sugar for textiles with Japan. (11th)

Record of Inspection Along the Songhua River 99

River Waters Swell, Japanese and Puppet Armies Lose Their Power

Rural Areas Bankrupt, Commerce Declines, Righteous Armies Active

Harbin Dispatch: In mid-June, a reporter disguised himself and traveled by boat from Harbin along the Songhua River to the Fujin area for inspection. In the area along the river, the activities of the righteous armies were most prevalent in counties such as Xindian, Tonghe, and Huachuan. As a result, ships dared not dock and stay. Each river vessel on the voyage was mostly escorted by ships from the puppet Songhua River Defense Fleet to provide protection. The ship taken this time was protected by the warships Jiangqing and Jiangping, fore and aft. Investigations along the river revealed that the righteous armies near Huachuan were the most determined in resisting Japan. They repeatedly attacked Japanese and puppet troops and even sent letters inviting the warships to battle. The Japanese and puppet troops were unable to deal with them due to their unpredictable movements. In Tonghe, the atmosphere was tense. The puppet Songhua River Defense Fleet's "Enmin" and "Pumin" ships are currently defending the area. Xindian is a vital waterway to Bin County. When the righteous army leader Zhao Shangzhi and his troops launched a fierce attack on Bin County, they also planned to seize Xindian first to cut off the enemy forces coming to the rescue from Harbin. The puppet Songhua River Defense Fleet then dispatched the "Datong" and "Limin" ships to be stationed in Xindian for a long time to guard Bin County. Since then, due to the soaring river waters, many farmlands have been flooded. Farmers, distressed by the Japanese monopoly after a bumper harvest last year, suffered a sharp drop in grain prices, resulting in rotten grain in their warehouses. Further economic pressure left them unable to save themselves from poverty. They did not consider the flood a hardship. Moreover, with the river water too high, low-lying areas became swamps. The Japanese and puppet armies lost their power. Therefore, many farmers voluntarily joined the righteous army, carrying guns. This kind of action was entirely motivated by the phenomenon of national and familial ruin. If we can take advantage of the situation and make this national spirit endure forever in the Northeast, it can also help recover lost territory. The larger docks along the coast are Fujin, Jiamusi, Huachuan, and Sanxing. In the Huachuan area, the righteous armies are very active, and the Japanese and puppet troops come to search from time to time. Therefore, families with a little wealth have mostly moved to Jiamusi. The losses can be imagined. Japanese and puppet troops are stationed in Fujin, Jiamusi, Sanxing, and other docks, with strict precautions. However, various places mainly rely on agricultural production. This year, because of cheap grain hurting farmers, the rural economy has gone bankrupt. Farmers' purchasing power has declined, and commerce has declined accordingly. Merchants are unable to stock goods. Each purchase is only enough to last for a dozen days of sales. The internal fatigue is evident. The shipping industry is also far inferior to what it used to be. The number of passengers traveling up and down is few and far between. Except for recruiting workers in various places, hardly anyone goes there. Because grain prices are too low, grain merchants cannot make a profit and do not load and transport it, resulting in ships having no goods to transport. The Japanese-puppet joint Songhua River Shipping United Bureau has no solution and can only transport fuel needed for winter and the present on the return trip to provide relief. However, some ships still need to be suspended to maintain the status quo. (Northeast News Agency)

Disaster Reports Pour in From Various Counties in Hubei Province 100

Strange Winds and Locusts Arrive Together

Remaining Rice in Dried Fields is Devastated

Millions of Refugees in Disaster Areas

Hankou Correspondence: Disasters of floods and droughts in Hubei Province are nearly ubiquitous throughout the province. The number of people affected by the disaster is no less than millions. In addition to the floods and droughts, there are also the dragon disasters in Guangji and the locust plagues in Huangmei. After a rain on the 16th, the northeast wind continued for several days, devastating the remaining rice in the dried fields. Thus, there is also the so-called wind disaster. How can we, the lower people, bear this? Disaster reports and telegrams have poured in from various counties. A summary of these is as follows: (1) Jun County: Mountain floods broke out, and many fields were flooded. (2) Yun County: Mountain floods broke out, and the Yunbai Highway was damaged. More than 130 road-building laborers were washed away by the water. (3) Yunxi: Villages were completely submerged, and the autumn harvest is hopeless. (4) Zhushan: The flooded area is very wide, and the people suffered huge losses. (5) Zhuxi: Mountain floods broke out, and villages were completely submerged. (6) Nanzhang: Heavy rain caused the water level to rise, flooding the city walls. (7) Yicheng: The water depth was equal to the height of the city walls, drowning many people and animals. (8) Xiangyang: The dikes on both sides of the Xiang River overflowed, and the water depth on the plains was more than ten feet, completely submerging the crops and drowning countless people and animals. The eighth and ninth districts were particularly severely affected, and Fancheng was also affected. (9) Lichuan: The drought is very severe, and cries of hardship are heard everywhere. (10) Zhongxiang: It has not rained for a long time, resulting in a drought. The riverbank areas were also flooded. (11) Jingshan: Severe drought has caused the crops to wither. (12) Jingmen: The Banghetang section of the Xiangnan main dike collapsed, and all districts were flooded. (13) Tianmen: The main dike below Yuekou collapsed, and the flooded area was about 300 forts, with a water depth of five to ten feet.
