The City Chamber of Commerce Resolves to Establish a Special Advisory Committee 169

Appoints Yu Qiaqing and Four Others as Committee Members, Approves the Resignation of Wang Xiaolai and Wang Yansong from the Supervisory Committee

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce held its fourth Executive Committee meeting at 4:00 PM yesterday. Present were Executive Committee members Jin Runxiang, Yu Zuoting, Hu Xiyuan, Xu Jiyu, Ma Jiliang, Ke Ganchen, Chen Zheqing, Ma Shaoquan, Zheng Chengqing, Pan Xusheng, Zheng Zenan, and Supervisory Committee members Pei Yunqing, Fang Jiaobo, Luo Qinghua, Shen Tianxin. Chairman Yu Zuoting had previously withdrawn, and Xu Jiyu was publicly elected as temporary chairman. After customary procedures, Secretary Yan E'sheng reported on various important chamber affairs. The following motions were then discussed: (1) Regarding the resignation of Supervisory Committee members Wang Xiaolai and Wang Yansong, despite representatives' efforts to persuade them to stay, their resignation was resolute. The resolution was that as the two Supervisory Committee members were determined to resign and persuasion was impossible, their request was reluctantly granted, and according to regulations, alternate Supervisory Committee members Cheng Zhusun and Cheng Yujie would fill the vacancies. This would be reported to the party and government authorities for record. (2) Regarding the proposal by the Standing Committee to establish an Advisory Committee, including draft regulations for approval, the resolution was to approve. (3) Regarding the proposal by the Standing Committee to invite Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, Qin Runqing, and Bei Songsun to be members of the Advisory Committee, the resolution was to approve. The regulations and letters of invitation for the Advisory Committee are recorded below:

Regulations 170

Regulations for the Special Advisory Committee of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce: (1) To develop chamber affairs, the chamber, through a resolution of the Executive Committee, invites respected figures from the business community to establish an Advisory Committee. (2) Members of the Advisory Committee hold honorary positions. Their duties are to provide advice to the Executive Committee or the Standing Committee when consulted, or to independently offer opinions on various major commercial issues. However, they do not bear responsibility for implementation, nor do they act externally in their name. (3) The number of members of the Advisory Committee is set at five to seven. (4) Candidates for the Advisory Committee are nominated by the Standing Committee from former chairmen or standing committee members who have made significant contributions to the chamber, hold great prestige, possess outstanding talent and virtue, and are widely respected in the business community, and then appointed by the Executive Committee. (5) Advisory Committee meetings are not held on a regular schedule. They may be convened upon the invitation of the Executive Committee or the Standing Committee, or upon the proposal of two members of the Advisory Committee. (6) At Advisory Committee meetings, a chairman is temporarily elected by public vote. Executive and Supervisory Committee members of the chamber may attend and participate in discussions. (7) The term of office for Advisory Committee members is four years, but they may be reappointed. (8) If an Advisory Committee member is elected as an Executive or Supervisory Committee member of the chamber during their term and takes office, their vacancy will be filled by another appointment. (9) These regulations shall be implemented upon approval by the Executive Committee and amended in the same manner.

Letter of Invitation 171

Esteemed Sir, Zuoting and others, though inept, have been publicly elected to bear heavy responsibilities. Standing at the edge of a frozen abyss, we know to be cautious, constantly mindful of the danger of rotten ropes. Fortunately, we have the rules of Xiao He as models to follow. Examining past cases of the chamber, there was originally a category of special directors, filled by those with great prestige in industry and commerce, to prepare for consultations in advance and gather elders in one place. The method was good and the intention beautiful, and we can learn from past events. Therefore, based on this principle, during the fourth Executive Committee meeting, it was proposed that a special Advisory Committee be established in the chamber, and that former chairmen or standing committee members be invited as members of the committee to offer their valuable advice from their positions of retirement, enhancing chamber affairs and complementing each other. It was also proposed that, given Your Esteemed's seniority in the business community, great talent, and widespread respect throughout the city, You should be invited to be a member of the Advisory Committee of the chamber. The resolution was unanimously passed. We now enclose the full text of the nine articles of the regulations of the committee and respectfully invite You to offer guidance and resolve doubts. We rely on Your great wisdom and earnestly request Your agreement, so as to satisfy public expectations.

All Zhejiang Public Association Requests Suspension of Construction Special Tax 172

All Zhejiang Public Association telegram to Zhejiang Provincial Government: Respectfully to the Zhejiang Provincial Government, Zhejiang Province has long been known as a region with heavy taxes. In recent years, the implementation of various new policies has invariably relied on surcharges on land taxes, exhausting resources to catch fish, and the people of Zhejiang have felt increasingly distressed, leading to the tragic collapse of the rural economy today. The central government, concerned about the people's suffering, has repeatedly issued clear orders that surcharges on land taxes should not exceed one times the regular tax. Recently, the National Financial Conference also resolved to abolish surcharges on land taxes in various provinces and eliminate all exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies, transferring the stamp tax and tobacco and alcohol license tax, which belong to national taxes, to the local provinces to offset the reduction of surcharges and exorbitant taxes. Upon investigation, Zhejiang's land tax surcharges have many items, and the construction special tax, with an additional one yuan per tael of land tax and one yuan per stone of grain compensation, is the largest. In the previous period, it accounted for 55.6% of the surcharges, and in the next period, it accounted for 30.3%, nearly 45% of the total surcharges. Therefore, to alleviate the people's suffering and reduce surcharges, this surcharge should be abolished as soon as possible, so as to comply with the central government's clear orders and comfort the people's expectations. Moreover, this special tax was initially named the military special tax and was originally limited to one year. Later, it was changed to the construction special tax, which is inconsistent with the original plan and has lost the people's trust. Now it is allocated to the debt fund. According to the meeting of various departments, it cannot be reduced until the debt reorganization plan is completely completed. The counties are allowed to exclude this special tax when calculating the total amount of land tax surcharges to show that they are not violating the method of not exceeding one times the regular tax. In name, they are complying with the order to reduce, but in reality, they are collecting as usual. The people's resources are exhausted, how can they bear this heavy burden for a long time? Moreover, although this special tax has been designated as a debt fund, the annual revenue is only 3 million yuan. The expenses of Zhejiang's judicial system at all levels should be paid by national taxes. This has been proposed and approved by the Financial Conference, which can save 1.8 million yuan of provincial funds annually. Using this to replace the special construction tax for debt reorganization should be more than sufficient, which is both in line with the original allocation plan and can reduce the people's burden, a win-win situation. As for the expenses of the Provincial Public Security Bureau, which amount to more than 700,000 yuan annually, according to the precedents before 1928, there were special funds to handle it. From 1912 to 1926, it was paid from the shop tax and various police taxes in the provincial capital. In 1927, the police force was expanded, and a housing tax was added, all of which are documented. It seems unnecessary to list it in the provincial treasury to handle local public security with local taxes. Secondly, the telephone bureau run by the Construction Department has now merged with the Ministry of Communications Telephone Bureau. In addition to business income, it can save 800,000 yuan in expenses each year. Other departments and their affiliated institutions that waste provincial funds are not in the minority. If a policy of austerity can be implemented and ways can be found to abolish them, other surcharges can be gradually reduced. However, due to factual constraints, it may not be possible to merge them all at once, so our association has not dared to request the abolition of all surcharges, only requesting that the construction special tax, which harms the people the most, be suspended first as an initial measure to comply with laws and regulations to reduce land tax surcharges. The handling of it should not be difficult. Reducing the people's financial resources by one point is equivalent to leaving one point of vitality for the countryside. At this time of severe drought, we especially hope that the special government will be implemented to pacify the floating population and provide relief. The case was proposed and passed by the entire membership of the 10th Membership Congress of our association. We urgently telegram this matter, hoping that the government will examine and approve it, and order the construction special tax to be suspended from the next period of this year to alleviate the people's suffering. We await orders with the utmost urgency. Shanghai All Zhejiang Public Association.

Cigarette Business Committee Discusses Tobacco Tax Yesterday 173

The Cigarette Business Committee previously received a letter from the Tax Affairs Department of the Ministry of Finance, soliciting opinions on the unified cigarette tax. The committee convened a meeting on the afternoon of the 24th of this month. Those present were Secretary Dong, Section Chief Jiang, and Section Chief Tang of the Tax Affairs Department, as well as Committee members Qiu Tingsheng, Shen Weiting, Chen Maonan, Ding Baiquan, Bao Gengsheng, and British American Tobacco Company representatives Bai Xiji and Liang Fuchu, and Da Mei Tobacco Company representative Zhu Junqing. The meeting was chaired by Bao Gengsheng. The resolutions are as follows: 1. Regarding the tax matter, Zhu Junqing advocated maintaining the current two-tier tax system, which was seconded by Chen Maonan. The BAT representatives agreed with Huacheng and said that the current unified tax is too heavy. It would be best to reduce it. If it cannot be reduced, and if business still fails to increase after the summer, the government should be asked to reconsider the request for tax reduction. There is no inequality in the current tax rate, which has been explained by the Tax Affairs Department. Ding Baiquan said that the proposal of the Minzhong Tobacco Company and others advocates increasing taxes on upper-grade cigarettes and reducing taxes on lower-grade cigarettes. Now that taxes on lower-grade cigarettes cannot be reduced, they also do not want taxes on upper-grade cigarettes to be increased. Bao Gengsheng seconded Ding's proposal. Shen Weiting seconded Ding's proposal. It was resolved to maintain the current two-tier tax system and continue to implement it, and to ask the Chinese cigarette manufacturers' association to convene members in groups to solicit opinions on this resolution in order to make a decision. 2. The BAT representatives proposed that, regarding the conflict of interest between high-grade and low-grade cigarettes, each cigarette manufacturer should discuss it separately and submit the results to the Cigarette Business Committee for review and referral to the Tax Affairs Department. The resolution was to approve. 3. The monthly sales of hand-rolled cigarettes have reached more than 20,000 cases, and there is also a lot of smuggling and tax evasion, leading to the decline of machine-made cigarette business. Since they are both cigarettes, they should pay the same tax. The resolution was to approve. 4. Regarding how to dispose of 280 cases of confiscated cigarette paper, the resolution was to send a letter to the Tax Affairs Department, requesting it to ask the Customs Department to destroy all of the confiscated cigarette paper. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM.

Ji Zejin Discusses Japan's Cultivation of Tung Trees 178

Already Trying to Grow Them on Jeju Island This Year, Seeking to Monopolize the World's Tung Oil Market

According to Mr. Ji Zejin, director of the Guidance Department of the International Trade Bureau, yesterday, tung oil is a specialty product of China and is essential for the furniture industry and the anti-corrosion of automobile bodies. The number exported to Japan each year is quite large. According to last year's statistics, the amount exported to Japan reached 9,808 dan, worth 235,508 yuan. The Governor-General of Korea has decided to find ways to encourage the cultivation of tung trees in order to prevent this import. Although China has imposed severe restrictions on the export of tung oil seeds, Mr. Takahashi Shigetaro, the manager of the Seoul branch of Mitsui & Co., Ltd., had a plan to collect tung oil seeds and transplant them to Japan when he was working in China. He has now started trial planting on Jeju Island in Jeolla-namdo. If the results are good, he will encourage large-scale planting in the coastal areas of Jeolla-namdo. Japan is cultivating tung trees and developing the tung oil industry in an organized and planned way using scientific methods, and its progress will naturally be rapid. Soon, Japan will be able to be self-sufficient in tung oil and will not need to rely on China. In the future, it may even export it to Europe and the United States and monopolize the world's tung oil market. Now, after several years of effort, the Japanese silk industry has captured the markets of China, Europe, and the United States. In a few years, I am afraid that China's tung oil market will also be seized. This shows the efforts of the Japanese, and the Chinese people must pay special attention to it. (New News Agency)

The Customs Office Considers Dried Seafood from the Coast to Be Japanese Goods 180

Ship Owner Reports to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Requesting a Letter to the Jianghai Customs Office for Certification

The two sandboats, Jin Deyuan and Jin Xinghe, from Hupu, loaded more than 400 pieces of dried fish, each weighing about two dan, from Dage Mountain and Zhangzi Island (both islands) in the Northeast. Because this year's production was not prosperous, the two ships were not even half-loaded. They arrived in Songjiang the day before yesterday and reported to the Jianghai Customs Office in Paotaiwan (also known as the Huangchuan) as usual. When the customs officers went to the two fishing boats for inspection, two old copper plates with the words "South Manchuria Railway" and a few small boxes of Japanese-made matches and cigarettes were found on the ships. This caused the customs officers to suspect that the dried fish loaded on the two ships was from Dalian and planned to confiscate the goods. The crew explained that the copper plates were old and discarded items, but they were not discarded because of their copper material. The matches and cigarettes were indeed purchased from Dalian. Because Dage Mountain and Zhangzi Island are only separated from Dalian by a sea, after the daily necessities prepared in the ship were used up, they had to be purchased from Dalian. However, the dried fish loaded was indeed purchased from Dage Mountain and Zhangzi Island, and there are shipping lists and money order from the firm in that place as proof. The Customs believed that the list and other documents could not be recognized as sufficient evidence, so they reported the situation to the Shanghai Customs Commissioner for handling, so that the two sandboats had been in Songjiang for two days, but the matter had not been resolved, so it was not convenient to open the cabin for sale, and the intangible losses were already considerable. The shipowner reported to the Sandboat Association and the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, requesting a letter to the Customs Office, proving the above circumstances and releasing them quickly to avoid being innocently harmed. The intent of the government to be lenient to fishermen with dried fish is to exempt them from taxation. However, the loading procedures are extremely strict. All ships going to load dried fish must first report to the Shanghai Customs Office before sailing, then go to the Wusong branch office to sign before they can sail. After loading the dried fish, they must go to the Shidao Customs to sign back to Shanghai. If no dried fish is loaded, they must return to Shanghai empty, and they are not allowed to turn to other places to load other goods. The customs declaration procedures are very solemn, and they can never deceive the customs and secretly load Japanese goods.

Ping-Pong Lawsuit Decision 181

The Defendant's Ruling Deemed Invalid, Jiande Team Finally Wins the Lawsuit

The Zhonghua Jiande Society's ping-pong team previously participated in the Champagne Cup ping-pong competition organized by the Racecourse Tongren Club. The Jiande team captain, Lu Xiulu, hired lawyers Yang Ruinian, E Shen, and Yin Jingzhu to sue the competition committee staff members Li Hongfa, Lu Xiniao, Shen Dingyi, Shen Zhirui, Lu Hanjun, and Weng Shoufeng in the First Special Court for abusing their power and illegal ruling, and requested that the ruling of withdrawal be confirmed as invalid. The defendants also hired lawyers Jiang Yiping and Wu Baotai to defend them. The debate has ended, and the details have been reported in this newspaper. This case is a correction of errors in the sports world and is greatly related to sportsmanship and morality, so people in society attach great importance to the outcome of this case. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhang Qinglan of the First Special Court opened the Fourth Civil Division and announced the verdict, the main text of which confirmed that the withdrawal ruled by the defendant was invalid, and the litigation costs were borne by the defendant.

Since the Shanghai Loving-Kindness Children's Association agreed to take over the Zhabei Civilian Fosterage Home, it has been actively carrying out various procedures. Yesterday, the association held a board of directors meeting and resolved to officially take over on the first of next month. According to Chen Tiesheng, the general secretary of the association, the Loving-Kindness Children's Association has decided to officially take over the Zhabei Civilian Fosterage Home on August 1st, but if the other party is unable to complete the handover in time, it may be postponed to August 10th, which is not certain. The fosterage home has an old fund of 80,000 yuan and a monthly income of about 600 yuan, which is insufficient to cover the expenses of supply, affairs, and education. In the future, the Loving-Kindness Children's Association will provide an additional subsidy of 400 yuan per month. As for the title of director of the fosterage home, it will be held by Xu Jianping, the general secretary of the Loving-Kindness Children's Association. If Mr. Xu is too busy with the Ministry of Finance and cannot take care of it, then Chen Tiesheng, the deputy general secretary, will take the position. Wang Guanyi, a member of the association's board of directors, will be fully responsible for the educational aspect.

Jiejang Company's Qichun Wheel Hits Reef Upstream of Yichang 189

Ship Sent to Rescue; Cargo Unloaded, Passengers Safe; U.S. Gunboat "Palos" Sailed to Protect

The Qichun Wheel of the American Jiejang Steamship Company, which sailed from Shanghai to Chongqing on the morning of the 12th of this month, hit a reef 40 miles from Wanxian on the river surface at 10 a.m. on the morning of the 22nd. The company sent a ship to rescue, the cargo has been unloaded, and the U.S. gunboat sailed to protect. The details are as follows:

Rapid Water Causes Ship to Hit Reef: The Jiejang Company's ships specialize in sailing the upper and lower reaches of the Yangtze River. The Qichun Wheel, with a gross tonnage of 510 tons and a net tonnage of 291 tons, sailed from Shanghai on the morning of the 12th of this month with 200 tons of cargo and passengers to Chongqing. At 10 a.m. on the morning of the 22nd, it sailed to the river surface 130 miles above Yichang, about 40 miles from Wanxian, in a place called Shizhuangzi. Because the water flow was very rapid and navigation was difficult, it hit a reef.

Telegram Sent for Assistance: After hitting the reef, the shipowner, Aitison, immediately used wireless telegraph to seek assistance and surveyed the place where the reef was hit. The bottom of the ship was broken by the reef, and river water entered. The ship was stranded on the reef, and would not sink immediately. He immediately comforted all the passengers, asking them to maintain order and assuring them that there was no danger, and to wait quietly for rescue. At the same time, he telegraphed the head office in Shanghai to report the incident. After receiving the telegram, the Shanghai company telegraphed the Wanxian branch to quickly send a ship to rescue.

Ship Sent to Rescue: The Wanxian branch immediately sent a barge to the scene of the accident to rescue. At the same time, the Yi'an Wheel, which sailed from Chongqing to Shanghai, received the telegram en route and rushed to the rescue at full speed. The barge arrived the day before yesterday, and the Yi'an Wheel arrived yesterday morning. They are currently working together to rescue. The Qiping Wheel, which set off from Shanghai on the 20th of this month, has been equipped with towing equipment in Hankou and is expected to arrive at the scene of the accident on the 27th. At that time, if the Qichun Wheel has not yet escaped danger, the Qiping Wheel will engage in towing rescue.

Cargo Unloaded, Passengers Safe: The Shanghai head office received a telegram yesterday morning stating that the Qichun Wheel was loaded with approximately 200 tons of goods, including cigarettes, foreign sundries, and mail. The cargo has been unloaded by the rescuing barge. As for the passengers, they are all safe. The unloaded goods and passengers will be transferred to the Yi'an Wheel and sailed back to Wanxian and Chongqing. There was no loss of passenger and crew luggage, only some of the cargo was water damaged.

Gunboat Protection: The American gunboat "Palos," which is stationed in Hankou, has sailed to the scene of the accident to protect the Qichun Wheel and prevent bandits from taking the opportunity to loot. It arrived yesterday and is parked next to the Qichun Wheel for protection.

Minimal Losses: A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency met with a Chinese staff member of the shipping department of the Shanghai head office yesterday morning. According to the interview, the Qichun Wheel hit a reef, the cargo has been unloaded, and the passengers are safe, so the losses are minimal. Only some of the cargo was water damaged. As for the Qichun Wheel, it will be towed to Shanghai for repairs in the shipyard after it is rescued.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and Others Jointly Run Chinese Bookkeeping Training Course; Enrollment Is Enthusiastic 193

The Improved Chinese Bookkeeping Training Course jointly organized by the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and accountant Xu Yongzuo aims to train talents in improved Chinese bookkeeping. The meeting hall of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce is used as a classroom, and accountant Xu presides over the teaching affairs. It is scheduled to start on August 1st and graduate at the end of September. Since registration began on July 20th, enrollment has been very enthusiastic, and most of the students are business staff. It can be seen that improved Chinese bookkeeping has generated a deep need in the business community. There are no age or gender restrictions for admission. Anyone who is literate and has some accounting experience is qualified. When registering for admission, students must take an examination in Chinese and abacus, but those who have been certified by industry associations or companies as being literate and having accounting experience can be exempted from the examination. Recently, many people from various industries have been submitting letters of recommendation to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and accountant Xu's office, and their purpose is to train accounting staff in order to improve bookkeeping. It is reported that classes are held from 7:40 a.m. to 8:40 a.m., which does not interfere with regular duties. The fees are very low, only 2 yuan per person for tuition, plus 2 yuan for textbooks and practice booklets. It is truly an excellent opportunity for those who aspire to learn bookkeeping. Accountant Xu's office is currently printing a large number of account books and forms for practical use in the training course. It is said that strict principles will be adopted in the training in the future so that students can obtain the general theory and skills of improved Chinese bookkeeping after graduation, go out to serve the society, and be able to perform their duties satisfactorily.

Rice Boat Owners Meet to Discuss Wharf Donation and Shenghe Issues 195

Yesterday afternoon, rice boat owners from various ports in the south gathered at Yizhichun in Nanshi to discuss wharf donation and rice unloading Shenghe (a type of commission) matters. It was discussed that in 1930, the rice industry purchased and built a dedicated rice industry wharf in Xuejia浜, Nanshi. Due to the large expenses, the rice industry resolved to collect a wharf donation of 1 cent per stone as construction costs, which would be stopped when fully collected. Although this donation was collected from the rice industry in the interior, the rice merchants in the interior hired boats to transport rice to Shanghai and repeatedly instructed not to deduct wharf donation from the rice money of the trade and repeatedly sent letters to Shanghai rice merchants and brokers for negotiation, but with no effect. Therefore, last month, rice industries from various ports in the interior came to Shanghai to convene a joint meeting of rice merchants and boat owners, requesting the bean and rice industry association to publicly announce the accounts of the wharf donation. If they do not comply, the wharf donation will be stopped from July. The wharf donation is still being collected. Therefore, the rice merchants in the interior instructed to hire boats to transport rice to Shanghai. If the wharf donation is extracted again, the rice merchants in the interior will not recognize it and ask our boat owners to be responsible. This matter affects the transportation of our boat owners. After discussion, tomorrow all boat owners will gather at the Rice Merchants Association to report the situation of the rice industry in the interior that refuses to bear the wharf donation because there is no accurate and detailed account announced and request to negotiate and stop the collection. Secondly, the issue of reducing Shenghe was discussed. Requesting the cargo owners in the interior to reduce Shenghe caused disputes, and a standard should be set as soon as possible so that there will be no loss in the future. After discussion, please ask the rice merchants to mediate with the interior.

Cured Madman Given Funds to Return Home 201

Previously, the Hongkou Police Department apprehended an unidentified madman on Wusong Road, who was extraordinarily deranged. He was sent to the Shanghai Mental Hospital affiliated with the Chinese Mental Hospital, next to the Dongyouheng Road small vegetable market in Hongkou, for treatment. After more than a month, he was completely cured, his mind clear. He recounted his wandering experiences, explaining that he came to Shanghai to visit relatives and seek employment, but due to an unclear address, he became a street vagrant, begging for a living. He further mentioned his elderly mother, wife, and children at home, who had no means of support, causing him excessive anxiety and mental disorder. As he spoke, he was moved to tears, which was quite pitiful. Therefore, the hospital purchased a boat ticket for him and provided funds to return to his hometown, so as to avoid wandering in a foreign land and to reunite with his family. This is truly great fortune for the madman.

Robbery Attempt Fails, Letter Sent Demanding Extortion of 3,000 Yuan 203

Suspects Arrested, Interrogated Yesterday

Li Xiamao's residence at No. 1 Daqing Lane, Rongji Road, Laobaidu, Pudong, a foreman for coal and miscellaneous goods, was broken into by four bandits around 9 PM on June 9. The robbery attempt failed, but they shot and wounded Du Shenghong, the bookkeeper employed by Li, in the leg. On the 27th of that month, Li received several threatening letters from the bandits, demanding 3,000 yuan. Li reported this to the Municipal Public Security Bureau. On the 9th of this month, Detective Team Leader Lu dispatched squad leader Gu Liancheng, along with detectives Shen Jinchu and others in disguise, accompanying Bai Xiaochun, the representative of Li Xiamao, to the designated location on North Sichuan Road, pretending to negotiate. They managed to apprehend two members of the gang, Li Changgen (alias Gong Ziliang) and Liu Xiuqing. They were transferred to the local court for questioning. Details have been reported in previous issues. It is now known that after the case was solved, according to the apprehended suspects, their accomplices were Zhu Changlin, Yang Youfa, and Xiao Chen. However, when attempts were made to arrest them, they had already fled without a trace. Yesterday morning, Inspector Lei Binzhang of the court ordered squad leader Gu Liancheng, detective Shen Jinchu, and Bai Xiaochun, the representative of the victim, and Du Shenghong, who was shot during the robbery, to appear in court to testify about everything that happened and how the suspects were apprehended. The interrogator then ordered the two suspects, Li Changgen and Liu Xiuqing, who were in custody, to be brought in for a lengthy interrogation. Three Notices from the Hydrographic Office 209

Navigational Notice No. 98 (Provisional Notice) from the Hydrographic Office of the Naval Department states: The lighted buoy of the "Donggou" new channel of the Gaoqiao Sandbar at the Yangtze River Estuary, Shanghai Port, on the east coast of the Republic of China, has been moved. Date of movement: July 20 of this year. Provisional position: Approximately 150 feet east on the chart. Explanation: The lighted buoy of "Donggou" will be temporarily relocated to the above-mentioned position on the above-mentioned date. Note: When the dredging work is completed, it will be moved back to its original position, and no further notice will be given at that time. Relevant charts: Hydrographic Chart No. 508 of the Naval Department. Reporting agency: Shanghai Customs.

Navigational Notice No. 99 from the Hydrographic Office of the Naval Department states: The depth of the navigation route of Baimao Sandbar at the Yangtze River Estuary on the east coast of the Republic of China has decreased. Position: From the "Tangqiankou" beacon, 24 degrees north and 2.34 nautical miles away, i.e., approximately 121 degrees 11 minutes east longitude and 31 degrees 42 minutes north latitude. Explanation: The depth of the navigation route between the "Baimao Sandbar South" buoy and the "Baimao Sandbar South Port South" buoy has now decreased. The depth at the above-mentioned position is 21 feet. Navigation caution: Before the above-mentioned buoys are relocated, all ships should pass eastwards from the above-mentioned reduced depth. Note: Chart No. 141 of the Naval Department has been corrected regarding this change. Relevant charts: Chart No. 141 of the Naval Department. Reporting agency: Hydrographic Office of the Naval Department. Note: The directions listed in this navigational notice are calculated from 0 degrees true north, turning clockwise to 359 degrees. However, the direction of the lights is calculated from the sea. The light range is based on clear weather. Fog signals are only used in foggy weather. If necessary, the depth recorded will be explained separately and calculated according to the largest scale chart, using the reference surface. July 19, 23rd year of the Republic of China.

The Hydrographic Office specially issued a notice regarding the movement of the Haibeigang Sandbar channel light buoy at the Yangtze River Estuary. Date of movement: From July 23. Its new position is 286.5 degrees north of the "Changfusha" beacon, 2.73 nautical miles away, i.e., approximately 120 degrees 31 minutes east longitude and 32 degrees 5 minutes north latitude.

Four Banks Reserve Treasury Issues Reserve Report 211

No. 237

The Four Banks Reserve Treasury is jointly established by the Yanye, Jincheng, Zhongnan, and Dalu Banks, specializing in issuing Zhongnan Bank banknotes. According to the treasury's issuance regulations, banknotes are issued with full reserves. Cash reserves are at least 60%, and guaranteed reserves are up to 40%. The 237th announcement of the Shanghai Reserve Treasury on July 21, 23rd year is recorded below: Amount of banknotes in circulation: 23,395,487 yuan. Military Yearbook Published 212

The Military Yearbook is compiled based on the reports and investigations of various national governments obtained by the League of Nations over the past ten years. The content includes the status of 64 member states of the League of Nations and non-member states, and details their organization and establishment. It contains records on the army, navy, and air force, military orders, military administration, military regions, military supplies, military expenses, organization, conscription, training, and mobilization of various countries, and also touches on the people's army, police, population, national borders, coastlines, railways, and other items. At a time when military competition is becoming increasingly fierce and the scourge of war is becoming increasingly urgent, the translation and publication of this book is sufficient for the study of the Chinese people. The book is a thick volume, hardback five yuan, paperback three and a half yuan. Published by the Inside and Outside News Agency, distributed by the Modern Bookstore on Simalu Road, Shanghai. All branches in various ports are on sale.

Reading Q&A

Scientific Rainmaking vs. Setting Up an Altar to Pray for Rain 221

Guiding Teacher:

I have a question that I would like you to answer. Although this is not a question from a textbook, it is closely related to our pursuit of knowledge. I think you will not be reluctant to teach, right?

According to reports, this year's heat has broken the record of the past sixty years. If it doesn't rain again, then the land will be scorched, and the drought will be very frightening.

China is a country that relies on the heavens for food. However, in recent years, the heavens have been making things difficult for her. Natural disasters and man-made calamities have followed one after another, so that people in power and the public have been busy praying to gods and Buddhas: When imperialism comes to invade, a Kalachakra Dharma Assembly is set up; when floods overflow, a Kalachakra Dharma Assembly is also set up; now, a drought has formed, and in addition to the Kalachakra Dharma Assembly, Zhang Tianshi is setting up an altar to pray for rain.

The concern of those in power and the public for the suffering of the people is something that I do not need to elaborate on. However, the question is: Is this kind of praying for rain helpful to the facts?

The 20th century is the age of science, not the age of theocracy. If rain can be prayed for, why would the heavens go to the trouble of creating such a drought? Moreover, Zhang Tianshi himself is a person who has a home but cannot return. Many of the followers of the Panchen Lama have died of heat in this hot weather. He cannot even protect himself, how can he protect others? Not long ago, scientific spirit mediums were discovered in the city. Everyone understands that this is a kind of superstition, somewhat close to spreading rumors to deceive the public. But isn't the current setting up of an altar to pray for rain better than scientific spirit mediums? Compared to the two, although the methods are different, the essence is the same. Why do people in society not only not expose its superstitious effect, but even praise it? Are they all deceived by the good-sounding term "praying for rain"?

It must be known that setting up an altar to pray for rain is just using the name to collect money. It is absolutely impossible to seek effectiveness. The hard-working people of the whole country, under the attack of heaven and man-made disasters, will only sit and wait for death if there is another drought. We can no longer be superstitious, we need scientific relief!

It is reported that Soviet Russia has invented a scientific method of praying for rain. If you know this method, I hope you will immediately disclose it, because although this will not immediately attract the attention of those in power and launch a large-scale scientific rainmaking experiment, it can somewhat give a considerable blow to some superstitious people and make the public know that only scientific rainmaking can save the drought, and all superstitions are deceptive!

I eagerly await a reply! Zhu Ming Chunqiu

Imperial Incense Drifting Record 222

—Original by Princess Der Ling, Translated by Qin Shouou

Because from childhood, she was assigned to be the wife of the son of the Empress Dowager's brother by her parents—that is, the Empress Dowager's nephew. Unexpectedly, when everything was ready and the wedding date was chosen, her fiancé suddenly died. According to the customs of the old Chinese era, although she had not had a real marital relationship with her fiancé, she still had to marry him and stay a widow for him, never thinking of marrying another person again. And the title of "Young Mistress Yuan" was ultimately added to her head! She was only a naive and lively little girl of eighteen at the time, but nominally, she had become a very bitter little widow in mourning! The cruelty of the old Chinese ethics is indeed an undeniable fact. When I met her in the palace, she was exactly twenty-four years old: but her demeanor was no different from that of an old woman in her forties or fifties. In her life, it can be said that there is no more happiness or joy! She was absolutely not allowed to talk to any man, nor could she laugh loudly casually; and she had to stay in the palace forever, until her soul left her body. But one thing was her fortune! That is, her nature was very stupid and taciturn, and she had almost no knowledge of life, so although her environment was so desolate and sad, she seemed not to feel it at all.

The other female officials were all girls from the close relatives of the emperor's surname, with nothing special to remember.

As for the duties we female officials undertook, it can be said that they were extremely easy. All our work was to serve the Empress Dowager: but we did not need to serve the Empress Dowager in matters such as dressing and combing her hair. We only took turns standing close to the Empress Dowager in pairs, and saying whatever came to mind, interesting words would do; but we all knew that it was very easy to get into trouble talking to the Empress Dowager, so we always let the Empress Dowager speak herself, but we pretended to listen with great interest, and carefully responded accordingly when she raised any questions. (90)

Dusk by the River 223

— Shazhou

When the mercury on the thermometer stretches straight to the top, the house is really like a fire bucket, so hot and stuffy that you can't breathe. By evening, you can no longer be confined in the house, as if there is too little air in the house.

Going to the river has been our slogan for the past few days.

Whenever the sun is about to set, we always walk slowly with three people or two families across the streets of this small city to the open riverbank. At that time, some of the large ships have already turned on their lights, and the river water is usually calm, without wind or waves. The twilight clouds in the sky are also quiet, as if they have been tired after being steamed by the sun all day, and the fire snakes that flicker flicker in the cloud eyes, but there is no sound of electricity.

It is certainly not just our small group who are enjoying the wind on the river, but this beautiful scenery seems to be specially made for us. We talk and laugh, and it seems that the day's bitter heat has disappeared into thin air at this moment.

When the big ships have gone far away and the sky and the river can no longer be distinguished, we slowly walk back, but still looking back at the fishing fires on the riverbank, as if we are reluctant to leave. When will I be able to live by the river and not leave? I thought.

When I walk through the streets of the small city again, the women are sitting on the road, naked and wearing a small bib, waving a palm fan and teaching the children to sing the "Firefly" song.

"...Today poor, tomorrow poor, picking up gold turns into copper." The firefly song sung by the children is bitter.

Swimming and Ear Diseases 224

— Huang Yingdai

In hot weather, because people can't stand the heat, those who can swim will jump into the swimming pool or nearby waterways to swim. However, before entering the water, we must first have some common sense about swimming. Swimming in the swimming pool is most likely to cause problems with the ears, either because the pool water is turbid or because we don't pay enough attention after getting out of the water. The best method is to plug the ears before entering the water, and the most common thing to plug the ears with now is medicated cotton.

Now is the time for swimming, but we must know that the result of ordinary swimming, especially in turbid water, is most likely to cause ear ulcers. This kind of event may not necessarily happen in a swimming pool with perfect equipment and clean pool water, but people who have had ear ulcers are most likely to have them ulcerated again after swimming. Sometimes it will also affect the nasal passages, causing tonsillitis catarrh and other symptoms, especially after suffering from scarlet fever or similar diseases in early years, when the ears have had problems and have been cured, swimming in the water is most likely to cause ear disease to recur. However, healthy people will not develop diseases as a result of swimming.

Here, there is also a very important thing, which is that when swimming, jumping into the water from a high place, the transmission of the shock force, from the nostrils to the eardrums, will damage the eardrum. Moreover, some people say that according to the results of general research, when jumping into the water, landing feet first is more likely to be affected by the shock force than landing head first, like ordinary diving. Regarding this point, it may make people suspicious, but it is very obvious why the stimulation of water is more severe when jumping into the water than diving, because diving has the head blocking the nasal passages.

If we say that, is swimming not very easy to cause ear ulcers? However, we only need to consider in advance whether we have always had ear ulcers. If not, then it will definitely not ulcerate. Moreover, the preventive methods are now known to everyone. Just put medicated cotton in your ears before entering the water to swim, so that the ears will not be immersed in water and ulcerate.

Four Company Commanders of the Northeast 225

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Thirty-Two: The General Amuses Himself with Pleasure All Day Long; Few Soldiers Return Amidst the Weeping of Young and Old

The next day, the concubine went out to play mahjong. One of her trusted old maids went to the grain store across the street to buy some good glutinous rice to cook porridge for the Master. Seeing the back door open, she said, "Shopkeeper, do you have any empty rooms in this back courtyard?" As she spoke, she walked toward the back courtyard. Lady Jiang had spoken to her once before, so she welcomed her into the house and said, "Please sit down. Aren't you from the Master Commander's house across the street?" The old maid said, "Yes! Our concubine sees your house from the window upstairs every day. That young lady is..." Lady Jiang said, "That's my daughter." The old maid smiled and said, "Our concubine is also young and likes to make friends with young ladies. She saw your daughter and likes her very much, so she asked me to come over and invite your daughter to come over and play." Lady Jiang really didn't expect the Master Commander's concubine to want to befriend Guizhi, so she smiled and said, "Oh my! How dare we? Our child doesn't understand anything. How can she go to meet people? Don't let your concubine laugh at her." At this time, Guizhi was the most clear-headed. She thought about the Master Commander's two smiles when they met, which were definitely not unintentional. Now, this old maid's invitation was from the concubine to come over and play. She is such a noble person that the Master Commander has to put on a performance at home just to appease her little temper. Why would she want to connect with me, a poor woman? Putting these two situations together, she could tell that this matter was mostly fake, so she interjected in the house, "Thank her for me. I'm feeling very unwell today and can't go out." Although Lady Jiang felt it was a pity to give up this opportunity, her daughter's pregnancy was more important than connecting with the Master Commander. So, she didn't dare to force Guizhi to go and said to the old maid, "This child of mine really doesn't lie. If she says she can't go out, she definitely won't go out." The old maid smiled and said, "Could it be that your daughter thinks the concubine's invitation isn't good enough and wants the first wife to invite her? But our first wife doesn't live here. Where can we find the first wife?" (441)

Little Tea Boy 226

— Cheng Zhao

A Mao is a new tea boy this semester. The Dean of Academic Affairs assigned him to serve students and teachers downstairs in the new building. He is very short and thin, with withered little hands and a sallow, bloodless face, obviously due to malnutrition. Usually, we can easily see him struggling to carry two buckets of washing water into the dormitory on his narrow shoulders. His swaying and trembling body is really pitiful.

Logically, children like A Mao should be sitting comfortably in the classroom, listening to lectures and being irrigated by the sweet dew of education. But his father is a carpenter, and the reward for his daily hard work can only barely maintain his own life. How can he afford to send A Mao to school? So A Mao was excluded from the gate of the university, selling his weak body to serve students and teachers, and he will be a tea boy for the rest of his life!

Sometimes, A Mao stands in front of our classroom, eagerly watching our happy situation in class. Sometimes, he stays at the window of the dormitory, watching our self-study life. He is so curious and envious that he forgets his duties and is scolded by the Dean of Academic Affairs.

On the eve of the graduation exam, just as the students were working hard to prepare for their lessons, there was suddenly a disturbance. It was said that the little tea boy, A Mao, had been scalded by boiling water. When we went to see, he had already been carried to the hospital by the school workers, leaving only a large pile of muddy water by the fence of the playground!

Miscellaneous Talk

Gua Sha (Skin Scraping) 229

— Zhang Yian

Gua Sha, this seems to be a not very civilized medical technique, but the experience of facts makes me have to adopt it.

I used to know and not believe that Gua Sha and other medical techniques would have any effect, and I was a little disgusted. The most important reason why I hated Gua Sha was seeing the red and black streaks all over the bodies of people who had been scraped, on their eyebrows, necks, chests, and backs.

Since that year, about six years ago, which was the year I started playing with photography, I tried the taste of Gua Sha. At that time, I had just learned to develop and print photos myself, so I filled a pavilion room as a darkroom. The summer light is the most convenient season for photography. Every day, the sunshine time is extended, and the light is particularly strong. You can also use a high-speed shutter to capture very high-speed movements without worrying about insufficient exposure. But this season is the most unsuitable for developing and printing, because the temperature is high, and there is often a risk of film melting, and working in a closed pavilion darkroom in the hot summer is not a very comfortable thing. My darkroom has a cement flat top on the upper level and a kitchen below. At noon, the strong sun bakes the cement top layer hot, and the kitchen below is cooking. As a rule, it is not allowed to work under such circumstances. However, I, who had just learned to develop and print, was extremely enthusiastic. Not to mention such weather, I would do it even in Africa, as long as there was a way to keep the film from melting.

One day, two days, three days, after working in the darkroom like this, I felt something different in my body: the joints of my shoulders, elbows, and knees felt like they were being pressed by thousands of pounds of weight; my eyelids also felt like they had hooks on them, and it was very difficult to open them. My head felt empty; my tongue felt tasteless when I ate because it had a coating. I just wanted to sleep, and I still didn't want to open my eyes when I woke up. I told my wife about my symptoms, and my wife said that I had heatstroke. So, ten drops of medicine water, Shanjii Pills, and other things were taken out and used.

Ten drops of medicine water are suitable for emergencies. This is not an emergency, and I don't feel anything after taking it. I feel a little better in my stomach after taking Pujii Pills, but my eyelids are still heavy, and my joints are still sore. This went on for two or three days, and I didn't eat for two or three days.

"Let's try Gua Sha," my wife suggested. Sister Xu, a female worker from Yangzhou, immediately agreed.

Although I have always hated Gua Sha, I couldn't resist their repeated encouragement and the oppression of pain, so I finally hardened my heart and gave it a try.

The equipment and medicines used for Gua Sha are very simple: a cup of hot water or hot tea, a spoon, or a copper coin. Tea water can sometimes be replaced by raw oil, and copper coins and spoons can be replaced by thin jade pieces such as jade earrings.

The person who gave me Gua Sha asked me to strip naked, and she wet the copper coin in hot water and started scraping. First, start from the back. You have to sit down and bend your back. In order to support the weight of your upper body, your hands naturally press on your knees. The first few scrapes don't feel like much, but if you really have "sha", then after a few scrapes you will feel a kind of bone-piercing pain. It is said that that is when the "sha" comes out. When the "sha" comes out, the skin starts to turn red. If the "sha" is heavy, the color will not only turn red, but also form purple-black blisters. From the spine, to the shoulders, to the arm bends, to the eyebrows. For the eyebrows, don't scrape the surface, but pull it. When I had Gua Sha for the first time, I jumped up in pain and almost couldn't finish it. But after the scraping, all the pain in your body disappeared immediately. Although this thing seems uncivilized, you can't help but believe it. After this time, because of my excessive enthusiasm for photography in those two years, I had to scrape several times every summer.

I can't explain with science why Gua Sha can cure heatstroke, but I have gained my factual belief.

Education News

Ministry of Education Orders Students Not to Apply to Unregistered Private Schools 230

丨 Schools Not Approved for Establishment and Unregistered Schools Should Also Not Be Applied to

Universities and Colleges Should Not Enroll Students Promoted from Unregistered Secondary Schools

(Nanjing, 24th) The Ministry of Education ordered various departments and bureaus, saying that students must not apply to private schools that have not been approved for establishment and are unregistered, and universities and colleges must not enroll transfer students from unregistered universities and colleges, and students promoted from unregistered secondary schools. This has been repeatedly ordered and announced in various cases. Recently, it has been reported that graduates of unregistered senior high schools can still apply for further education first, which is obviously contrary to the methods set by the Ministry. In order to avoid misunderstandings, the previous order is hereby reiterated that the schools must not enroll transfer students from unregistered universities and colleges and students promoted from unregistered secondary schools. If they violate the order and enroll again, the Ministry will not recognize them. They are hereby ordered to transfer the order to provincial and registered private universities and colleges to strictly comply.

Municipal Education Bureau Informs Private Schools That They Can Only Enroll Students After Being Approved to Open 231

Private School Regulations Have Been Revised　Registration Procedures Are Divided Into Three Types

A public letter from the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau states: "I hereby inform you that the regulations for private schools have been revised and promulgated by the Ministry of Education. According to the revised regulations for private schools, the procedures for applying for registration are divided into only three types: (1) the founder submits an application to the school board for registration; (2) reports the opening of the school; (3) applies for school registration, etc., which is slightly simpler than before. However, newly established private schools must follow the provisions of Article 26, Paragraph 1 of the regulations: 'Schools must not enroll students before being approved to open by the competent education administrative authority.' In the future, if there are newly established schools, they must be approved to open by the bureau before they can enroll students. A copy of the revised regulations for private schools is enclosed for your reference."

Find a Way to Employ

(Nanjing, 24th) Representatives of students and workers of Peking University went to the Executive Yuan on the 24th to receive instructions. Ministry of Education Orders Attention to the Reporting of Staff and Student Rosters 233

The Ministry of Education issued a circular to the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities on the 23rd, stating that Articles 9 to 12 of the Secondary School Regulations, Articles 12 to 15 of the Normal School Regulations, and Articles 15 and 16 of the Vocational School Regulations all have clear provisions regarding the timely reporting of various matters related to teachers, students, school funding budgets, school rules, school buildings, and equipment. At present, among the rosters of public and private secondary schools submitted to the Ministry by the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities, there are quite a few that conform to the regulations, but there are more that do not conform to the regulations. It is very difficult to review them. In addition to the styles of rosters for the various matters that schools should report, which will be revised and promulgated separately, the following special regulations are made for the points that are most easily overlooked and erroneous in the staff and student rosters reported by the schools, so that they can be followed.

(1) The principals and directors should be in charge of teaching and should not receive separate salaries. The rosters should indicate the departments and years of service, as well as the subjects and hours currently taught.

(2) The directors of moral education, citizenship, or party doctrine teachers should be employed by those who have passed the examination or review. The rosters should indicate the time of examination or review and the certificate number.

(3) Teachers of each subject should be hired as much as possible by those who specialize in that subject. The rosters should indicate the departments they have studied, the number of years they have been teachers, and their teaching performance.

(4) The calculation methods for student grades should be handled separately in accordance with the regulations. The graduation examination results should be handled separately in accordance with the graduation examination regulations for secondary school normal students. The rosters should indicate the calculation process and results. (5) The start and end times and names of academic years should be handled in accordance with the school's calendar. For example, those after August 22 should be called the first semester of the 22nd academic year, and those after February 23 should be called the second semester of the 22nd academic year. They should not be arbitrarily named, so as not to violate the regulations.

(6) Some schools are only now reporting the rosters for the 19th academic year, which is too late. They should quickly submit all subsequent academic year rosters to make them complete. From the 23rd academic year onwards, they must follow the regulations and not delay.

The above are all the matters that schools should pay attention to when handling rosters. The departments are instructed to follow them. At the same time, the departments should also pay attention to the following points when submitting the rosters of various schools.

(1) If the rosters reported by various schools do not conform to the above items, they should be rejected immediately. If there are special circumstances that allow for appropriate changes, they should also add specific notes for review. They should not be transferred hastily before the department has carefully reviewed them.

(2) Attention should be paid to the number of teachers and students, the number of students in each grade, the teaching subjects, and the allocation of funds. If there is any non-compliance, it should be corrected at any time.

(3) The staff and student rosters of private secondary schools that have not been filed with the Ministry should not be transferred by the departments. If the junior high school has been filed but the senior high school has not been filed, the junior high school part should be reviewed and transferred, and the senior high school part should be returned. If the teachers and staff of the senior and junior high schools cannot be divided, the junior high school part should be re-created and submitted.

(4) When the departments transfer the various rosters of various schools, they should submit them directly to the Ministry without having to submit them to the provincial and municipal governments for consultation, in order to speed up the process. If it is necessary to submit them to the provincial and municipal governments for filing, they can also be submitted separately at the same time.

The investigation and reporting of rosters by various schools is extremely important. The education administrative authorities can know a glimpse of their handling status based on the rosters reported by the schools. Among the schools, there are those whose reported rosters can still barely meet the requirements, but the content of the handling is not completely consistent. If the reported rosters are already wrong, it is rare to expect them to be handled legally. In the future, if the departments find that the rosters reported by various schools are still in compliance with the regulations, they should not regard them as sufficient. They should still pay attention to whether the actual situation of each school is consistent with the reported rosters. The rosters sent by each school should be checked against the reports provided by the supervisors of the department from time to time to facilitate supervision. If any non-compliance is found in the rosters sent by each school, they should be ordered to be changed immediately, and attention should be paid to the actual situation of the school at any time to urge improvement. It should be known that although there are many reasons for the success or failure of schools, they are generally related to whether the allocation of funds is appropriate, whether the hiring of teachers is appropriate, whether the moral education is carried out appropriately, and whether the management of students is conscientious. Now that various regulations have been promulgated, there are standards to follow for how schools should be run. The departments bear the heavy responsibility of organizing local education. The review of school rosters is a preliminary work of a universal nature and must be strictly followed. This is of utmost importance. This order.

Three Provincial Headquarters Advocate Production Education 234

All Ordinary Schools Should Implement the Half-Farming and Half-Studying Doctrine

Regulations for Implementation are Issued to the Three Provincial Governments for Compliance

(Hankou Communication) In order to implement the production of education, the Commander-in-Chief of the Three Provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui has formulated measures and issued instructions to the three provincial governments on the 23rd, ordering the two departments of construction and education to strictly comply. In general, ordinary schools in various places should formulate education policies separately by administrative organs and education organs, according to the needs of the local area and the personality and family status of the students. The general principle is to pay attention to the production of education. The implementation methods are as follows: (1) Each school must set up a school garden, supervise students to cultivate various crops by themselves, practice on the spot, and may set up agricultural farms or forestry and animal husbandry farms by using the organization of cooperatives, with teachers and staff leading students to plant and raise livestock, and implement the doctrine of half-farming and half-study. All income, except for expenses and payment for the purchase or lease of land, may be distributed to teachers and students to encourage them. (2) Each school must set up a specimen room, lead students to collect local artificial and natural products, and display them for observation. (3) Add various cooperative knowledge to the citizenship course, add local products and methods to be improved to the geography course, add various knowledge of agriculture, forestry, sericulture, chicken raising, pig raising, and bee raising and improve skills to the natural course, and add methods to improve local industries and manufacture products for sale to the physics and chemistry and manual courses to promote them. (4) Advocate diligence and simplicity, cultivate the atmosphere of enduring hardship and not using school servants. (5) Local administrative organs and education organs must run at least one vocational school according to local needs, so that the school is industrialized, the students are apprentices, and the career is socialized. Based on this principle, the implementation methods must achieve the following items: A. The teaching materials used must be divided into two categories: one, taken from the local area; two, taken from other places, using scientific methods to compare the strengths and weaknesses and teach at the school to improve them. B. The practice time must be more than double the lecture time to cultivate the technology of all-round hands. C. During each semester, teachers and students must go to various places in groups once or twice to give tours and lectures, and guide farmers or workers on the spot with the results of their practice in order to improve operations.

Du Yannian's Speech at the Capital Women's Political and Legal Institute 239

The Illiterate Laborer Wang Fengyi Founded 500 Women's Schools

On the morning of the 21st, the Capital Women's Political and Legal Institute specially invited Mr. Du Yannian, Director-General of the Beijing Universal Morality Society, and Mr. Gao Pengjiu to give lectures. First, Ms. Liu Linghua introduced the recent developments in the East Asian women's rights movement, which are advancing rapidly. In Japan, a female farmer named Misuko founded the Tenrikyo Church, which already has more than six million followers. They are spreading their teachings in various countries around the world, with women accounting for the majority, while men are passively assisting. A few days ago, the head of the church, Masayoshi Nakayama, came to Shanghai and visited various girls' schools in Xujiahui, which was praised as extraordinary by both Chinese and Westerners. However, they were unaware that China also has an extraordinary figure who founded five or six hundred women's schools, namely Mr. Du Yanping and Mr. Wang Fengyi, the Director-General of the Universal Morality Society. Mr. Du is not so surprising, but what is surprising is that the only mentor of the society, Wang Fengyi, is an illiterate laborer who was able to found five or six hundred women's schools. This is truly a great light in China's women's rights movement and a precursor to global female harmony, which is unique in the world. Therefore, we specially introduce her to our school, so that we can connect with the brilliance of the practitioners of the Universal Morality Society.

Next, Mr. Du spoke about how the society was founded in Shandong in the tenth year of the Republic by the prodigy Jiang Xizhang. In Jiang's vernacular interpretations of the Four Books, he often praised Mr. Liu Renhang's method of transforming families into villages, so they have known each other for a long time. This time he came to Shanghai to conclude the handling of the Shandong Yellow River flood disaster and was able to meet Mr. Liu. Now, with his introduction, I will report on the work of our society over the past ten years. In recent years, because the prodigy Jiang has often been abroad, Mr. Wang Fengyi, our mentor, and I have been handling everything. We are greatly inspired by Mr. Wang's spirit. Mr. Wang has no other strengths, but he is a poor man from Chaoyang, Rehe. He worked as a hired laborer when he was young and is illiterate. However, after being ill for twelve years, he suddenly heard someone preaching the section on Shuangguan Gao from "Picking Up the Lost," and his illness was cured. The reason was that his family was arguing, and each member, including the grandparents and daughters-in-law, repented and reunited. Mr. Wang thus realized the method of repenting with a clear conscience to cure illness. After he was cured, he went everywhere to persuade people to cure illness, not by using spells, but by directly pointing to their original heart. As a result, thousands of people were cured, and it became popular in the three northeastern provinces. Mr. Wang also made a vow to help virtuous people with chivalry and to sacrifice his life to save virtuous friends. After making this vow, he unexpectedly saw the world illuminated in the middle of the night and realized the great way. However, Mr. Wang's realization is very special. He realized that the root cause of social chaos lies not only in national politics but must start from transforming the family, and not only in men but also in women and children. Therefore, he never runs schools for boys or universities but specializes in running elementary schools for girls to cultivate motherly education as the foundation of everything. He also uses his special inspirational power to persuade women to manage their families harmoniously, treat their parents-in-law and sisters-in-law well, and teach their children well. If the family is at peace, the men will naturally be good. Mr. Wang is illiterate, but whenever families in various provinces have difficulties, if they ask our society to send someone to persuade them, the problems will be resolved. This is all due to Mr. Wang's special inspirational power. Therefore, the work done by our society is purely based on foolish sincerity, practicing the feminine way of gentleness and inspiration, and has no other strengths. This is very different from the modern emphasis on improving women's rights but focusing on equal distribution of inheritance, etc. Currently, our society has cultivated 160,000 women and has run three or four hundred elementary schools in the Guandong region and one or two hundred in Hebei, Shandong, and other provinces, all using this method. I also have no knowledge or academic expertise to lecture, but I am just reporting what we have practiced for the public's reference. Practitioners will definitely not look down on women and children, and they will practice female gentleness to inspire men to be upright. The way is very easy. Everyone must know that although there are many people in the world, they are only men and women. Using male force to control men is not as easy as using female gentleness to transform them. This is what our mentor Wang has personally experienced and practiced. His ideas can be considered a practical and effective implementation of Mr. Liu's advocacy of female harmony. This is a special report. The audience applauded enthusiastically. Next, Mr. Gao from the society spoke. I have served in the military and political circles for many years and have been the head of various counties in Jiangsu and Shaanxi. At first, I thought that having power would definitely lead to success, but later I realized that having power does not necessarily have practical results. Therefore, I realized the importance of Taoist transformation. Currently, our society is developing industries in the Northwest to support the poor. Due to time constraints, I will not say more.

Next, Ms. Huang Dianhua spoke. I have been running schools for girls and boys of all levels for many years. However, I am deeply interested in Mr. Wang's natural awakening to transform society, with an emphasis on women and children, which is something that the general public has not thought of. Your society practices using female harmony to transform male strength, which truly confirms Mr. Liu's theory of female harmony. In addition, I also have a new economic policy to assist moral transformation, which I will discuss in detail another day.

Finally, Mr. Tong Boting, the director of the Capital Women's Political and Legal Institute, expressed his gratitude, and the meeting ended happily.
