Free Talk

Treat Jokes as Just Jokes 259

— Comberdo

Unexpectedly, Mr. Liu Bannong suddenly passed away, and the academic community has lost another person. This is something to be regretted. But I know nothing about ancient phonology, so I am not qualified to say a word of praise or criticism. Instead, I am reminded of another matter. When the current vernacular was about to be "abandoned" or "despised," he was also a great "head-on attacker" of the current vernacular, especially the Europeanized vernacular.

He once had a brilliant article that was effortless but very powerful:

"I will now give a simple example:

Confucius said: 'To learn and constantly practice it, is that not a pleasure?'

This is too old-fashioned, not good! 'To learn and constantly practice it,' Confucius said, 'is that not a pleasure?'

This is good!

'To learn and constantly practice it,' 'Is that not a pleasure?' Confucius said. This is even better! Why is it good? It's Europeanized. But 'Confucius said' ultimately could not be Europeanized to 'Said Confucius'!"

This passage appears in "A General Theory of Chinese Grammar," which is a serious book. The author was also a colleague of "New Youth," a fighter of the "Literary Revolution" in the May Fourth era, and now he has become an ancient person. According to the old Chinese custom, death can often increase value, so I would like to bring it up again and point out that he was also a colleague of the "Analects" Society and sometimes could not help but make some "jokes." Originally, he also had "humor," but these "jokes" often fell into the gutter of "joking."

The actual example is the article quoted above. In fact, that argument is no different from the words of stubborn gentlemen and street rascals who, when they see young people wearing foreign clothes and learning foreign languages, sneer and say, "It's a pity that your nose is still low and your face is not white."

Naturally, what Mr. Liu opposed was "too Europeanized." But what is the scope of "too"? The first three methods he cited do not exist in classical Chinese, but they can exist in conversations and can be understood by people. Only changing "Confucius said" to "Said Confucius" is definitely incomprehensible. However, he could not find a real example in the Europeanized articles he opposed, so he had to say that "'Confucius said' ultimately could not be Europeanized to 'Said Confucius'!" Isn't this "shooting at a target that isn't there?"

The main reason for the intrusion of Europeanized grammar into Chinese vernacular is not because of curiosity but because of necessity. National essence scholars hate foreign airs, but when they live in the concession, they will write strange place names like "Avenue Joffre" and "Avenue Haig." It is not that the commentators want to be strange, but to be precise, the existing vernacular is not enough, so they have to adopt some foreign syntax. It is true that it is relatively difficult to understand, unlike tea and rice that can be swallowed in one gulp, but the compensation for this shortcoming is precision. Mr. Hu Shi's "Ibsenism," published in "New Youth," is indeed easier to understand than some recent literary essays, but don't we feel that it is also superficial and vague?

If those who ridicule the Europeanized vernacular, in addition to ridiculing, try to introduce foreign precision works without arbitrarily changing or deleting them, I think they will still be able to give us better advice.

Using jokes to deal with enemies is naturally also a good tactic, but the point of contact must be the opponent's fatal wound. Otherwise, a joke is just a joke.

Dispersing Melancholy 260

— Feng Zi

These past few days, Shanghai has been extremely bustling. Christians are praying to God, Buddhists are chanting scriptures, and Taoists naturally have to join in the fun. So they invited Zhang Ruiling, the 63rd-generation ancestral master from Longhu Mountain in Jiangxi, to set up an altar and perform rituals to eliminate disasters and pray for rain. The Living Buddha has just left, and now the Heavenly Master has arrived. If China is to face any more so-called disasters, only Heaven knows what will happen.

But disasters certainly exist. Let's not even talk about the political and economic ones; even the farmers, who depend solely on agriculture for their livelihoods, are suffering. A bumper harvest can become a disaster—this was the experience of last year. In the past, when the rice was about to ripen, one only needed to inquire at the teahouses in town to find out if any neighboring counties were experiencing famine. Then, whether you were Uncle Nine-Catty or Auntie Seven-Catty, you could predict the price of grain. But this hasn't been the case in recent years. There's drought in the Northwest and major flooding in the Yangtze River. Grain prices should be high, right? But the opposite is true. Even the predictions of rice merchants who are familiar with the national situation have fallen flat. The reason is that there's Siam in the South, Taiwan in the East, India in the West, and steamships crossing the Pacific Ocean. These places all produce rice and can freely transport it to China.

As a result, foreign rice floods the market, and rural areas go bankrupt. This has also become a disaster. The Living Buddha and the Heavenly Master certainly have no "magic" to dispel it, and the philanthropists haven't even thought about it.

However, the farmers are certainly not lacking in benevolence. Didn't Nanjing have a financial conference? The aim was to abolish excessive and miscellaneous taxes and not increase land taxes. It hasn't been long since we remember that. But what is the actual situation? Taking my hometown as an example, the collection is divided into two installments. The regular tax is four national currency units per mu (approximately 1/6 of an acre). In the first installment, surcharges such as the construction special levy, construction surcharge, special levy collection surcharge, autonomous surcharge, education surcharge, pest control expenses, and collection fee amount to a total surcharge of one yuan and forty-seven cents and nine li (one-tenth of a cent) per yuan. In the second installment, surcharges such as the construction special levy, special levy collection surcharge, construction surcharge, surcharge collection surcharge, pest control expenses, party fee surcharge, vocational training institute expenses, and collection fee amount to a total surcharge of nine dimes and five cents and six li per yuan. That is to say, for every yuan paid in regular tax each year, you still have to pay two yuan and forty-three cents and five li in surcharges. However, compared to last year, this has already been reduced by a few cents, showing that it has been affected by the financial conference after all. But the exception is that this year there is also a so-called surveying and mapping fee of twenty-five cents per mu. The land has not yet been surveyed, but the expenses have already been collected in advance. Just as a few cents are reduced, several dimes are added. Their skin and flesh are already gone; the farmers' spines will probably be broken to be sold as firewood.

This has naturally become another disaster. The Living Buddha remains indifferent, the Heavenly Master silent, and everyone is ultimately speechless.

But Shanghai is bustling after all. Gentlemen shed a few more drops of sweat, and then drought became a disaster. Living Buddhas, priests, Heavenly Masters, ascended the altar and sat in their seats, praying devoutly, and sweet rain indeed fell generously, although it is not known whose merit it was.

After the rain, the air is newly cool, and the gentlemen nod to each other and say, "It's so refreshing! It's not at all gloomy these days."

But the gloom still exists, just like the disaster. It is hidden in another group of people.

The Contradiction Between Morality and Writing 261

— Dun Pang

Anecdotes from the Qing Dynasty Literary Scene, Part 3

Wang Xizhuang (Wusheng) had not yet passed his examinations and was tutoring in a wealthy family's home. Every time he entered the house, he would make a gesture of scooping up something with both hands. When people asked him about it, he said, "I want to scoop the wealth and prosperity of this family into my own embrace." After he became an official, he engaged in deception and misappropriation, taking many things for himself. When people asked him, "Sir, you are rich in learning, yet you are so greedy and stingy. Are you not afraid of how posterity will view your reputation?" He replied, "Greed and stinginess are only temporary ridicule, while learning is a legacy for a thousand years. I am confident that my literary fame can be passed down through the ages. A hundred years from now, word-of-mouth reputation will have faded, but my writings will still exist. My morality and writing will still be there." Therefore, his writings are full of passionate and stirring words, which were meant to conceal his greed and vulgarity.

Note: This excerpt is enough to prove the greatness of literature, and also enough to prove the freedom of literature. A greedy and vulgar person can use his writing to express his lofty morality a hundred years later—this is the greatness. A greedy and vulgar person can create passionate and stirring writing, which shows that there is no relationship between character and literature, let alone economic conditions and class consciousness—this is the freedom. However, conversely, it is inevitable that people feel "disillusioned." If the literati of the past were like this, then can we really trust the literati of today who write elegant or revolutionary words—can we really trust their elegance and revolution? Morality and writing are often contradictory, and examples abound.

The Mountain Hermit Who Helps Out 262

— Dun Li

Anecdotes from the Qing Dynasty Literary Scene, Part 4

Chen Meigong encountered an official at the home of Wang Jingshi, who asked Jingshi, "Who is this person?" Jingshi said, "A mountain hermit." The official said, "If he is a mountain hermit, why doesn't he go to the mountains?" He was mocking him for being under the patronage of a nobleman. Soon they sat down at the table, and the official gave an order, "First, a black name; second, two sentences from the Four Books; and last, a line from a drama that fits the meaning." The official first cited, "Ten sisters married eight brothers; eight mouths can be free from hunger; but who will the two daughters rely on?" Meigong said, "The painted-browed thrush has married the white-haired old man; I am old and cannot use it; I have wasted my youthful years." The whole assembly praised him, and the official then became friends with him. Jiang Chaosheng, a compiler from Qianshan, wrote a play called "The Dream of Linchuan" with a scene called "Hidden Treachery," intentionally vilifying Meigong. His entrance poem says, "Decorating the mountains and forests with great pretension, attached to elegance, a minor celebrity. Without trying to take the Zhongnan shortcut, he boasts of being a recluse to an extreme degree. Using the sacrifices to otters to fill his writings, busily flies around cauldrons and tripods to moisten the mists and clouds. Lightly, a cloud crane, flies back and forth, rushing to the Prime Minister." It is also mocking and abusive.

Note: This excerpt can be compared with the previous excerpt. Many people today admire the temperament and style of the literati of the late Ming and early Qing dynasties, but they do not realize that the mountain hermits and celebrities of that time were nothing more than helpers of the nobles. Nobles cannot do without this kind of person, so although the official initially mocked Meigong, he eventually "became friends with him." And this kind of person cannot become a mountain hermit and celebrity without leaving the nobleman, so Meigong was mocked but did not take offense, and he also eventually "became friends with him." Jiang Xinyu exposed the ugliness of the "celebrities" who were "attached to elegance," and some people think it is mocking and abusive, but who knows that they themselves do not care at all? But those who are attached to elegance today do not actually not know these situations, but they are just such people themselves.

Sweat 263

— TK

Memories of Lake Biwa in the Shadows 264

— Sheng Maliang

The gentle sunlight bathes the morning of Lake Biwa.

A small boat floats in the tranquil lake, and my mood is as calm as the lake water.

Yinzi and I are often intoxicated here, with such a gentle breeze and such a quiet reflection on the waves...

The light boat glides slowly on the tranquil lake, are the tones of the waves the poetic intent forgotten by poets?

Beautiful cloud shadows drift lightly by, and Yinzi's memories bring up old dreams of her hometown: the sky in Pyongyang also has such light cloud shadows!

Oh, young man! You, will you recall your hometown in China?

Oh!...

Sadness is hidden in the faint dimples of her smile. The two of us are both people adrift in foreign lands. Oh, Yinzi, you are like a drop of dew on a duckweed!

(Forget it! That desolate hometown!)

Silently plucking the strings of my mandolin, the wanderer sings a wandering song:

"The old ripples only reflect the old dreams,

The wanderer only sings the wandering song,

Oh, the returning swallow, does it bring a gentle breeze from the old land?

Stop recalling the vanished rose-colored dreams,

Oh, how many times have I wandered!

The moonlight of the old land is vaguely hazy..."

My heart is like a quiet ripple. A white gull swoops past, and ripples stir again.

On the distant shore of the lake, a young Japanese girl walks by. Her fluttering clothes are so light and carefree in the shadow of the wind!

Silently, Yinzi leans in my arms, telling of the sadness of wandering. The emotions of a traveler are so poignant!

A white flower is tied in Yinzi's hair, and a fragrance drifts in the wind.

Three years have passed.

Now, the old shadows of Lake Biwa are faint, but the life of the past three years has flowed like mud, and there has been no news of Yinzi!

The wanderer's heart stirs with even deeper pain. Oh, life is just a dream. Silently, the mandolin strings play mournful sounds. Sing, let the lost youth live as an old dream in the shadows of memories!

"Stop recalling the vanished rose-colored dreams,

Oh, how many times have I wandered!

The moonlight of the old land is vaguely hazy..." (June, 1934)

Watermelon 265

— Chen Zizhan

Watermelons as big as human heads are carried in baskets to the homes of the privileged. The watermelons are frozen at the bottom of the refrigerator, and the electric fan blows like a cold north wind. The maids, dripping with sweat, bring out the watermelons. Slicing watermelons is always easier than killing heads. The master, madam, young miss, and young master all come together, everyone eats watermelon and leans back on the sofa.

X X X,

If watermelons also had mouths, they could say a lot of complaining words: "The countryside gives me life, the city squeezes me dry. Those who give me life, year after year, don't know how much blood and sweat they've shed; those who squeeze me dry, on such hot days, I don't see a single bead of sweat on them. Each of us is like a human head, killing us is more terrible than killing human heads."

I Come From the East (6) 266

— Xingye

Most of the women can ride wild horses, and most of the men know how to use guns. They are more straightforward than the Americans in the East, more revolutionary, and love adventure and resistance. After the Indians were eliminated, they used the method of overcoming foreign races to overcome the oppression of nature. Railways were built; minerals were developed; canals, dams, roads, and underground oil pipelines all quickly appeared in this barren area. And the construction projects seen in this area, such as the Hoover Dam and the border dams, can best represent the vigorous vitality of the American nation.

As the car drove further, approaching the Rocky Mountains, the desert nature of the fields became more and more severe. The mountain slopes are made up of yellow ash soil. Whenever a strong wind passes, yellow sand flies down from the mountains in heavy clouds. The air is so dry that I feel like I am traveling below the pyramids of Egypt. The moist winds of the Pacific Ocean cannot blow here because they are blocked by the mountains, and this place is far from the Gulf of Mexico. Although there are a few farmlands in the sand dunes, they can only grow barley and rye. Mexicans, wearing wide-brimmed straw hats and riding breeches with large legs, often appear in the wilderness. They still retain some of the manners of ancient Spanish knights and the hereditary blood of red Indians. Their rough and dark faces, paired with hard and black beards, sing Mexican love songs with great satisfaction. The southwestern provinces of the United States were originally taken from the hands of the Mexicans, so there are still many Mexicans living in the southwest of the Rocky Mountains.

Although the Rocky Mountains are tall, their scenery is far less beautiful than Yandang Mountain in eastern Zhejiang. The eastern foot of the mountains is very simple and straight. The pine trees are lined up like electric poles, without any twists and turns. Several very sharp mountain peaks are still covered with white snow, like white hats. Although there are large streams under the mountains, I have not seen a single beautiful waterfall along the way. The car turned on the top of the mountain for several hours, slowly taking me to the western foot of the Rocky Mountains. The air here is very clear, and in this May weather, the green forest covers everything on the mountain. The car route winds through the green shade, and red houses can be seen vaguely along the road, most of which are wealthy people's summer villas. Within ten miles of Salt Lake City, everything contains fresh poetry. A large group of sheep slowly came along the foot of the mountain, facing the car. The driver had to stop and let the sheep squeeze past the car, rubbing against it. When the sunset had filled the mountains, the cherry trees in the mountains, the small lake under the trees, and the white geese swimming on the lake were in harmony with each other. Salt Lake City is built in the mountains. The streets are very clean and wide. The cleanliness and tidiness of the buildings are rarely seen in the United States. Only a few decades ago, the area around Salt Lake City was still a barren wilderness covered with yellow sand and roamed by Red Indians. Later, the leader of the Mormon religion led some men and women who were not afraid of hardship, pushing clumsy and heavy ox carts, and came across the Rocky Mountains. They suffered drought and locust plagues; they fought with brave foreign races and fought with the cruel pressure of nature. They began to build an irrigation system, turning countless deserts into fertile land. Now, the Mormon Church still displays many relics of the pioneers and all the pictures of the opening up. If you go to visit, they will carefully entertain and guide you.

Many Japanese immigrants live here, and many Japanese who grew up in the United States have almost been assimilated by the United States because they do not know how to write Japanese characters or speak Japanese. Many Japanese restaurants are open on the street, and the prices of the food inside are always very cheap. The local Americans, on the one hand, hate these short Easterners, and at the same time, they are very afraid of them. Compared with the Chinese expatriates, they are more self-conscious. They know how to unite and know how to protect the dignity of the country. At the Salt Lake Hotel where I was staying, the boss asked me what part of Japan I was from. When they knew I was Chinese, he gave me friendly advice, saying that in this area, you should call yourself Japanese. It is conceivable what the word "Chinese" evokes in the minds of Americans.

Thirty-Three Silk Factories Opened in This City 286

In recent years, the silk factory industry has been on the verge of bankruptcy. Before the new cocoons came on the market this year, only about a dozen factories were barely working. After the spring cocoons were shipped to Shanghai, various manufacturers planned to resume operations. After detailed investigation, a total of thirty-three silk factories in the city have successively started work as of now, including Baotai, Xiangcheng, Fengda, Xiangyu, Huafeng, Xiesheng, Xinglun, Fuchang, Yuncheng, Dafeng, Fengtai, Meifeng, Meisheng, Junshengfu, Hongsheng, Hengcang, Dingchang, Yongheng, Xingchang, Dexing, Yutong, Yuanxing, Yufeng, Xuchang, Yutai, Chongyu, Yifeng, Fulunheng, Yuji, Gongda, Guangyuan, and Henglong. Among them, most are short-term in nature, renting factories to reel silk. The lease term is only set for 3-4 months. If there is a futures market after the term, they will extend the lease with the factory owner and continue working; otherwise, they will stop work and close down.

Random Thoughts

Professional Alliance and Professional Petition 290

— Wei

Recently, university graduates in Peiping have formed a professional alliance. Its purpose is to demand employment from society. At the same time, representatives have been sent to Beijing to petition the central government for employment. This can be said to be a novel event in society recently.

The lack of career prospects for university students is not a recent phenomenon, but it has become more pronounced recently. In the past, most university graduates could still find some employment, even if it was not a good job and was often unrelated to their field of study, but at least they could find employment. But this is not the case recently. It seems that unemployment is the default for university graduates. Therefore, some people say that graduation is unemployment, which is not without reason. From this point of view, the career prospects for university graduates are much more difficult than before. The organization of a professional alliance by university graduates in Peiping, and further petitioning the central government for employment, is not without reason.

The lack of career prospects for university students shows the extent to which China's economy has declined. The current extremely desolate economic situation in China is what causes the general feeling of a lack of career prospects among graduates. As the social economy declines more and more, all industries are depressed, and new talents cannot be employed everywhere, and even old talents are often kicked out. Naturally, there are even fewer career prospects for new university students. This is the reason why university students generally feel that there is no way out. If the social economy continues to decline in this way, future graduates will feel the pain of having no career prospects even more. By then, I am afraid that not only will there be student professional alliances, but also larger-scale national youth unemployment organizations. However, unless the social economy improves, these organizations and these demands will be ineffective.

From the lack of career prospects for university graduates, we can see the extent to which the crisis of the entire Chinese nation has risen. The countryside is bankrupt, and national industries have been completely destroyed, leaving only the starving and cold people across the country. What a painful and terrifying situation this is. The lack of career prospects for university students, viewed in the context of the entire social problem, is only a small part of it. Other more serious problems at present, such as the total collapse of the national economy, are even more serious than this by ten or a hundred times. The lack of career prospects for university students is only one aspect of the surface events. However, even this small problem is enough to make us shudder when we hear about it. How will we deal with other more serious problems with an even more chilling attitude?

From the lack of career prospects for university graduates, we are also reminded of the issue of the sharp decline in the number of university applicants this year. According to surveys, the number of applicants for various universities this year has decreased significantly compared to previous years. This is not without reason. The total collapse of the national economy has also greatly reduced the number of students entering schools. This is a truly terrible phenomenon. In the future, I think there will not be many people left across the country who can afford to go to school. Universities are even less likely. What can those who have always advocated saving the country through education do about this?

Beat 291

— A Tan

Getting up early in the morning, the sun was already shining on the stinky water in the small river, spitting out bubbles. The train, like a lost soul, dragged its steps slowly and called out "woo". Si Xizi pulled Jin Guozi's hand and jumped off the sleepers, the grass basket containing the ice hitting his butt, his sister honestly putting her finger in her mouth and crying.

"You mother's little devils." The flagman guarding the iron gate waved the green flag and scolded affectionately. "Cry your mother's cunt, the train is afraid of not being able to crush you two little bastards."

!

Si Xizi pretended not to hear and walked past him, the train calling "Hurry! Hurry!" and chased past them. Gou Bao put the ice basket on his head and ran from the fork, gently slapping Jin Guozi on the ear. She deliberately cried loudly, holding her brother's hand and refusing to leave.

"Sister, let's go! Don't mind that dog." Si Xizi said.

"Si Xizi, I originally wanted to tell you something, but you just look down on people." Gou Bao put his hands on his hips, his eyes wide and round.

"Where does ivory come from a dog's mouth? I don't want to listen!" Si Xizi quickly walked away, pulling his sister's little hand.

"What are you doing, you always scold me?" Gou Bao chased after and asked.

"Did I scold you?" Si Xizi said with a smile, "Think carefully about your name. You're born of a dog, I'm even elevating you."

"Don't joke around." Gou Bao also laughed. Said, "Si Xizi, I met your mother yesterday! Oh, she's dressed so beautifully. Haha!"

"Where?" Si Xizi couldn't help but stop and asked! Since his father died, his mother ran away with someone not long after. Grandma the blind woman scolded him several times a day before she was willing to take Jin Guozi to beg for money. Earlier, Si Xizi and the other children were scavenging in the trash cans. The weather was too hot, and Grandma the blind woman had already fallen ill from the sun and couldn't move at home. Si Xizi and a group of little devils took advantage of this time to sell ice. Business was not bad, but Jin Guozi was too small to run, and she always cried when she thought of her mother. Si Xizi's heart broke when he heard this. Whenever he encountered a back view that looked like his mother, he always took his sister and shouted after them, selling ice.

"In the brothel!" Gou Bao said, flashing cunning eyes.

"What's a brothel?" Jin Guozi asked innocently, widening her eyes.

"Let's go, sister!" Si Xizi said, and punched Gou Bao's skinny, black face twice with a fierce look, saying, "You dare to make fun of me, do you recognize this?"

"Honestly, Si Xizi, I'm telling you the truth." Gou Bao chased after and said sincerely, "Little Sanzi heard that Little Cottage is also coming to sell ice. He doesn't even want to pay us respects, let's all beat this little brother-in-law."

"Is the rule made by you?" Si Xizi said more angrily.

"Are you insisting on going against us!" Gou Bao also got angry.

"If you want to go against you, then go against you, I bet you can't bite off my dick." Si Xizi was so angry that his neck turned red.

"Okay, you remember, beat this little brother-in-law!" Gou Bao said, running ahead and looking back at them fiercely even after walking a long way.

"Hurry, hurry up!" Zhao Di caught up with them at the Maigen Road station. Her yellow hair was draped over her shoulders, her gray and white short clothes fluttered in the wind, and there were several holes in her pants, revealing a pair of slender, bare legs. "Hey, Si Xizi, the sun is really good, it's already burning my skin, let's go quickly, Jin Guozi, good sister, it's getting late."

Why are you late too? Si Xizi asked.

"Ah, unlucky, unlucky. I passed by Little Cottage's house, and his mother is about to kick the bucket, lying on the ground moaning, asking for water! Little Cottage doesn't know where he's playing, so I had to pour her two bowls."

"Did she take any medicine?" Si Xizi said, "My father died because he didn't have medicine to take."

"She didn't take it either, the doctor from the epidemic hospital told her to buy it, but she doesn't have any money!"

"Whatever, if you want to beat him, beat everyone." She wiped her hands with her clothes. "Si Xizi, this must be Little San, I don't get along with him."

A String of Nonsense 293

— Wen Gai

The eyes of a proud person have already changed in structure. He can only see above and in front. If you call him from the side, he will say that he cannot see.

A person's self-esteem is necessary. Without self-esteem, he will not only be able to do the despicable things of flattering and fawning on others, but also like others' flattery and fawning the most.

People who flatter others like others to flatter them the most.

Self-esteem is the bodyguard of personality, and pride is a bomb that destroys oneself.

The person who has the clearest and most thorough understanding of life has already approached the gate of hell, otherwise he will do all kinds of evil without restraint.

A person who takes life too seriously has only one path to take, and that is suicide, otherwise, he will kill.

The person who talks about the philosophy of life with every breath only fails to understand what life is the most. Because he does not understand what life is, he falls into a state of distress and annoyance!

The person who does not understand what is called the philosophy of life is the happiest and lives the longest.

A selfish person is a suspicious person; he does not believe in others, nor does he believe in himself.

Only a person who loves himself can extend that love to others; a person who cannot extend love to others does not even cherish himself.

Robbed 294

— Gu Yue

Danxi, a peaceful and lovely village, with the sparkling Danxi River flowing in front of the village, and the Huangyan Mountain looming behind the village, which surrounds the west end of Danxi like a very kind and loving mother. During every summer evening, unrestrained laughter would secretly run out of the village, proudly echoing the song of the Danxi River.

Beautiful! I believe that in this world, nothing can compare to her except for the sweetest girl!

Who could have expected it? Danxi has been robbed in the past year! It has been destroyed beyond recognition, and the people in the village have gradually moved to other places. All that is left in the village is a deathly silence: Danxi has been robbed! This is the sin of society!

The situation of being robbed is very common. It is happening in almost every rural village. Obviously, the only reason is the inevitable phenomenon of rural economic bankruptcy.

One energetic morning, a terrifying message suddenly came: the outsiders living in the Xiyang Mountains, because they could not stand the pressure of hunger, decided to mobilize a large group of people to go outside the mountains to snatch rice that afternoon. The so-called snatching rice is not just wanting your grain, it is like robbers robbing, but the name sounds better!

The entire Danxi was also plunged into a terrifying darkness. In those villages without any defense corps, everyone felt that this robbery was a very easy thing; the people in the village knew that only their own strength could be relied on, so the village leaders issued an order for each person to protect their own home. Families without men were protected by their close relatives; those with guns took out their guns, and those with knives took out their knives to save this life-or-death situation.

So the entire morning was spent in preparation, and women and children were hiding in the houses and not allowed to come out, because there was nowhere to escape at all.

Time finally came, and the scout in front ran back sweating profusely to report:

"Damn it! There are really a lot of people! The men are in the front to fight, the women are in the middle, and the children are following behind; the men are in charge of robbery, all with knives and guns; the women are in charge of looting the house, all with ropes and kitchen knives; the children are in charge of taking things away and running, all with ropes and carrying poles; the men, women, and children are connected all the way from the Xiyang Mountains to the stone road outside the mountains, there are really a lot of people!"

The village chiefs held a temporary emergency meeting and decided to defend the stone bridgehead. As long as the vanguard was not allowed to rush in, everything would be easily resolved.

Chanting to boost morale while walking, the large team of robbers gradually approached the stone bridgehead.

"Give them a warning!" The guards at the bridgehead fired two shots into the sky.

"Don't be afraid! Charge up! We are going to starve to death, what are we afraid of?" The vanguard mustered their courage and rushed over in one breath.

Think about it, how can you resist so many people with five guns? Therefore, they finally rushed into the first line of defense.

The guards of the first line of defense retreated to the second line of defense, and joined forces with the people in the village to make one last stand, but they were unstoppable, and in less than a quarter of an hour, they rushed into the village entrance.

The village chief had no choice but to shout loudly:

"What do you want, brothers?"

"We have no food to eat!"

"Then, let's withdraw from the village and let you eat your fill! Okay?"

"That's also possible! We didn't want to hurt anyone in the first place!"

As a result, except for the guards in the first two waves, no one was injured, but the houses were looted clean, and the losses were countless!

The residents of Danxi, after suffering this major robbery,

moved to other places in a mess to find their way out, except for a few poor wretches who became lackeys.

The lovely Danxi, left with only desolation and loneliness, but the Danxi River is still flowing, and the Huangyan Mountain is still looming around.

Lonely Heart 295

— Min Jian

The sun was like a ripe apple, retracting its daytime radiance, like a shy bride, slowly pulling the surrounding white clouds over to cover her entire face.

At this time, the scenery on the earth all seemed very hazy and quiet, shrouded in a layer of gray veil. Sometimes, the calls of one or two crows flying across the sky punctuated the loneliness of the early autumn.

After a while, the sky became lively again, and the stars flickered with their brilliance as if competing for beauty, but no one was willing to make a sound, just lying quietly in the lonely black sky.

A breeze swept across the lake, causing the grasshoppers to chirp. I stared foolishly at the silent stars, intoxicated in the embrace of early autumn.

"Ah! What a beautiful early autumn night," I said, quite moved by the thought of returning home;

"The poplar trees that I planted in the yard five years ago must be towering trees by now. The swallows chirping under the eaves must have flown to the south by now. Also, the crickets under the bean trellis; they were called the orchestra by my sister, and now they must be playing their mysterious tunes there..." The scenes of my hometown floated into my mind like shadow plays, one after another.

The night is quiet, poetic;

A few desolate flute sounds came from the bamboo forest, and two or three fishing lights appeared in the reed pen, with the sound of oars hitting the water, suddenly awakening me, who was immersed in memories, and I looked aimlessly at the flickering fishing lights, unable to continue the memories I had just had.

The fishing boat was far away, the lights were gone, and the sound of oars no longer echoed. It seemed that the surrounding scenery had disappeared. What remained was only my lonely heart.

Amateur Mailbox

Low Fees 296

— Editor

Dear Editor:

I have a question concerning the safety of hundreds of thousands of women giving birth in Shanghai. Please take the time to publicly advise me, as if you were experiencing it yourself!

There is a K obstetrical hospital in Shanghai, with about six or seven branches, and no fewer than twenty female doctors who deliver babies. The scale cannot be considered small, and the delivery fees are particularly low, so it can meet the needs of middle and lower-class families! According to the hospital's regulations; the delivery fee is only four yuan; prenatal examinations and postpartum treatments are completely free, regardless of the number of times. However, the facts are completely opposite. The biggest problem with the hospital is the "blind injections" that are criticized by the general public in Shanghai! Regardless of whether the women giving birth need it, they always encourage them to get injections. The cost of the needle itself is often only a few corners, but the price is as high as five, six, or eight yuan per injection, so the hospital has made a fortune invisibly! And poor women giving birth, when there is a dangerous situation and they should get injections, but because the needle fee is too expensive, they cannot afford it, and can only wait for death. To give examples, I can't finish talking about it in a day. The hospital also has two shortcomings: (1) The female doctors who deliver the babies are very young and inexperienced, and they talk and laugh casually during delivery, with a negligent attitude, (2) The equipment and care are inadequate. Nurses come only once or twice a day and are not responsible for the babies. The bedding is not disinfected, and several women giving birth share an ordinary toilet, so it is easy for the women giving birth to contract serious diseases! I have a relative, Ms. Wang, whose family is not very well-off. She stayed in the hospital to give birth at the beginning of last month. A few days later, she got sick and was later transferred to a hospital in Ximen for treatment, but it was ineffective and she died. Another relative, Ms. Zhang, gave birth in the hospital at the end of the previous month. The injections alone cost more than twenty yuan. A week later, she also got sick and was later transferred to a hospital on Haige Road for treatment. She stayed in the hospital for three weeks and spent fifty gold yuan. Fortunately, she recovered. Now my two relatives are preparing to jointly demand compensation from the hospital for the losses, but my idea is to resolve it legally in order to effectively ban it.

Dear Editor: Do you think these two cases should be resolved privately or officially? If a lawsuit is filed, what kind of procedures are required? In addition to the diagnostic reports from doctors at the two major hospitals of Ximen and Haige Road as evidence, are other witnesses needed? Please answer the above questions, I am not the only one who is grateful! I wish you

Literary peace! Zhang Qingfeng, July 12

Answer: Your letter reveals all kinds of dark secrets in the business of slippery obstetrical hospitals in Shanghai, which is indeed a serious issue related to the safety of hundreds of thousands of women giving birth in Shanghai. In addition to expressing extreme hatred for these quack doctors who only aim to make money and do not care about people's lives, the editor also regrets that your two relatives lack knowledge of the dark secrets of Shanghai and only knew how to be greedy for cheapness, resulting in the loss of wealth and life. Further, the executive authorities in Shanghai who manage health affairs should also be held responsible for failing to ban and supervise these hospitals with inadequate facilities and poor management, resulting in countless lives suffering losses. This issue is highly valued in European and American countries, because it is not only related to the interests of the people, but also closely related to the prosperity of the country. In Shanghai, which has a population of 3.5 million, there are only a few public and municipal hospitals. How can they meet the needs of citizens? Although there are private hospitals with subsidies, the ones with perfect equipment are all priced very high, and only a few high-ranking officials, wealthy merchants, and big tycoons can enjoy them. Poor scholars can only sigh. Due to the needs of this environment, slippery hospitals that call for low prices naturally emerged. At first, they attract people with the lowest prices, and then they deceive people into getting injections with business skills. Giving birth is a very important matter, and life is in the balance. It is common for strong and healthy young women to lose their lives in a moment or three due to giving birth. So in that situation, the women giving birth only hope to get through the crisis safely and be safe, so they do not care about their various extortions. These hospitals are aimed at making money, only knowing how to seek profit, and they will not care about other people's lives and wealth. Based on the fact that these executive authorities have neither established public hospitals extensively nor strictly supervised and evaluated private hospital doctors, such a serious problem has been created. In a place with such a large population, the birth rate must be very high. Before you raised this issue, I don't know how many women giving birth have died at the hands of these quack doctors (old-fashioned midwives are even worse). Thinking about it, it is really frightening!

The shortcomings of the hospital you mentioned are not accidental based on the above reasons. As for whether the death and near-death of your relatives should be entirely the responsibility of the hospital, this of course needs to be determined based on whether the hospital has any negligence in its business. However, since you have diagnostic reports from two hospitals as proof, it can constitute the basis for litigation. As for what kind of procedures are required to file a lawsuit, it is best to consult with a lawyer, which is more appropriate. In addition, submitting a request to the municipal government and public bureau for strict banning is also a legitimate method, and both can be pursued at the same time. As for private settlement, since you believe that this is an issue related to the safety of hundreds of thousands of women giving birth in Shanghai, there is naturally no need to say more, and even if you settle with him privately, I don't think he will sell you the account!

Homecoming (4) 297

— By Bulgarian Ivan Vazov, Translated by Yang Sen

The peace treaty was signed.

Christmas was approaching, and the soldiers were about to be discharged. Several young men from Wittlern had already returned, but Stoyan was not among them. Indeed, there was no news of him. Mother Zuna gradually became uneasy, and painful thoughts assailed her.

The days passed, one by one: she often went to the door. Was someone knocking? Longuil. Stoyan Inov had returned: then came Dinkoov's son, followed by the Stamatov brothers. She sought them out, questioned them, but they knew nothing. Before a certain period, they had all seen Stoyan, but afterwards, none of them had seen him again.

"Mama, Demetrius is back," her daughter Qina shouted at her as she came home. So she went out again to see Demetrius.

"Hello, Demetrius. Where is Stoyan staying?"

Demetrius also knew nothing at all. "Perhaps," he said comfortingly, "they sent him past Vidin, and he will return by another road."

"Holy Mother, where on earth is my child?" she murmured.

She went to Stoyanga's house. At the door, her heart was beating violently. She guessed, undoubtedly, that Stoyanga would tell her news about Stoyan, that he had sent his greetings: and that he could be home before Christmas. But in fact, Stoyanga did not answer: she only remained silent, her eyes wet.

The whole town was in an uproar. They were waiting for the first regiment returning from the front to pass through here. Right in front of Mother Zuna's door, they had planted two trees, their branches intertwined to form an arch. Fragrant pine branches, brought from the mountains, were used to decorate the tree and the arch, and above them were signs, transported from afar from Bazargic, with the words: "Welcome our brave warriors!" Around the signs, there were countless Bulgarian tricolor flags, a veritable triumphal arch.

The victorious army arrived and passed through on time.

"Perhaps he will return a little later; he will certainly not spend Christmas in a foreign land. Stragglers are still coming, one after another. There are still countless moments until evening. He knows that there are countless anxious hearts waiting for him here."

That poor mother thought this way.

Shen Bao Local Supplement Film Special

Re-examining Cantonese Sound Films from the Perspective of "Mass Language" (Part 2) 298

— Tang Na

Mr. Danfeng says, "The mass language suitable for films is a very clear sentence like "What to do if it doesn't rain?" If this "clear sentence" is spoken to Cantonese people, won't it be difficult to understand even if it is not translated into Cantonese? Although Mr. Danfeng says "local color can be emphasized in pronunciation," this is really not advocating language unification, but rather advocating vernacular Chinese. In order to maintain local color, in China, where there is no unified national language yet, to have only differences in pronunciation, like a Scottish villager speaking English, is in fact acknowledging the necessity of the existence of dialect films. Mr. Danfeng also mentioned that the dialect of his hometown cannot be understood by the general public, and the problem inevitably extends to mass films.

At present, film is not for the masses. Now, film is still in noble, great buildings, serving as "eye-catching ice cream" for soft gentlemen. Art cannot exist if it is not for the masses. Dialect films! Drama! Literary movements are not separate from mass film! Drama! Literary movements. If the masses in Mr. Danfeng's hometown could not see films in the past, and now films begin to exist to meet their needs, would they understand these films if their dialect is not used? Or is it to promote the "national language" unification movement of the gentry, merchants, and compradors by using "clear sentences"? Or is it to make the masses understand reality, to organize and educate the masses by using dialects? Our answer is definitely the latter.

Mr. Danfeng believes that the mass language movement "is to liberate language and writing from vernacular Chinese, making it something that is easily understood by the masses." What exactly is the so-called "easily understood thing"? Judging from the example of "What to do if it doesn't rain?" cited by Mr. Danfeng, nothing has been explained.

"What to do if it doesn't rain?" This is a vernacular sentence, and a vernacular sentence that is easily seen in current film subtitles. But in sound films, this vernacular sentence, which is easily seen in current film subtitles, must be translated into Cantonese to be easily understood by Cantonese audiences, and the recording of this Cantonese will certainly not be the words "What to do if it doesn't rain?"

"Mass language should be liberated from vernacular Chinese," I think this does not mean that vernacular Chinese is not needed. In fact, the "liberation" in what Mr. Danfeng calls "liberating it, making it something easily understood by the masses" is difficult to explain. Judging from the example cited by Mr. Danfeng, it probably means that we should cleanse the "mule-like spirit" and "quotation style" from vernacular Chinese and accept the aspect that is developing and approaching the masses. This is correct, but the mass language proposal is more than just this step. Furthermore, this will not conflict with the promotion of dialects. Because the language that is most easily understood by the masses is not the classical Chinese written on paper that some people consider economical, nor the "mass language" written on paper that Mr. Danfeng considers clear, but their own living language that they use every day. And the "current" construction of mass language is not to immediately construct a spoken language that is commonly used by the masses nationwide. This cannot be achieved in one fell swoop in the "present." What we can do in the "present" is to promote the development of dialects and organize the "modern Chinese Mandarin" (in fact, Cantonese is accepting this Mandarin). And this is the advocacy of dialect film! drama! literary movement. "Now" the vast working masses are illiterate. To construct a mass language that is easily understood by the masses, including writing, reading, and listening, we must have a "movement to turn the spoken language of the masses in various regions into written language." Regarding this, I plan to discuss it further in the issue of film subtitles.

Finally, Mr. Danfeng says that we intellectuals are unwilling to delve into the masses, and the construction of mass language will not succeed. I would like to add a point, which is that the construction of mass language is not just a matter for us intellectuals, but also something that the masses do themselves.

Too much has been said. I hope everyone will correct me without reservation. (The End)

Film Review

Review of "Springtime for Henry" 299

— Yi Jun

Spring time for Henry

丨丨Great Shanghai丨丨

A consistently ordinary comedic film about love triangles and quadrangles.

Here, the true face of society is not revealed; on the contrary, the true face is covered up by scarlet love.

Originally, we are not saying that films cannot be made with love triangles and quadrangles as the subject matter. We can reflect the true turbulent face of society in the love entanglements of men and women in triangles and quadrangles.

But in general, in ordinary American romantic comedies, can we find any social truth?

I remember "Waterloo Bridge," starring Heifley, which was shown at the Tai Guang last year. Although it used the pink entanglement of love as its theme, the playwright could not help but touch on the truth of society and slightly mentioned the situation where poor parents had no choice but to give away their children.

But even these playwrights who slightly see the truth of society are rare. In general, playwrights not only do not go to see the truth of society, but they also try to cover up the truth with pink dreams.

"Springtime for Henry" is no different from ordinary American romantic comedies.

Even though the director achieved some success here, the more powerful his partial success, the more it covered up the truth. And some places are over the top, such as Henry taking off his formal suit and putting on a quilt, etc.

Among the actors, Charlotte Greenwood is the best, and Nancy Carroll is also very good.

Song of the Fishermen: Reasons for Box Office Success 300

— Lao Sun

In the past, whether it was a Chinese or foreign film, it was already very rare to be able to show continuously at one theater for more than ten days. Therefore, when "Metropolis Morning" was shown in Beijing for eighteen consecutive days, everyone thought it was very strange. However, since "Sister Flowers" was shown continuously at the New Light for two months, it created a new record. However, its public screening happened to coincide with the Lunar New Year, and it also received a lot of so-called "timing" help. Now, the film "Song of the Fishermen" has been able to be shown continuously for more than a month in this hot summer, and it is said that it will continue to be shown. This can't help but be called a miracle in the Chinese film industry. Now, let me talk about the reasons why this film can be a box office success:

There are usually two sayings, saying "Those who perform in dramas are crazy, and those who watch dramas are fools." These two sentences are indeed very correct, and the more crazy one side is, the more serious the other side is. Taking "Song of the Fishermen" as an example, when it was released, if you mingled in the crowd and paid a little attention, you would hear many cries of pity coming from the mouths of the audience. This is an expression of their being moved by the people in the play. Therefore, the sadness of the story and the authenticity of the performance are the biggest reasons why "Song of the Fishermen" can be a box office success.

The second level is that a drama's story must first have universality. In other words, it must make everyone able to understand the content of the story without feeling any awkwardness. For example, let's take foreign films as an example. Films like "Women" and "The Adventures of Don Quixote" are not as popular as ordinary films. There is no other reason, it is because the former has a deeper meaning, which cannot be understood by ordinary audiences. Then, taking the two films "Life" and "Song of the Fishermen" as examples, if viewed from an artistic standpoint, they are both excellent works in domestic films. However, because the meaning of "Life" is deeper, in terms of commercial gain, "Song of the Fishermen" finally won.

Let's examine the editing techniques of "Song of the Fishermen." Except for one or two shots that are slightly lengthy, it is completed in one go from beginning to end. Every frame is powerful, and every episode is stimulating. And the further it goes, the more intense it becomes, tightly grabbing the audience's hearts. This level is indeed worthy of praise.

There is also another level, that is, the success of "Song of the Fishermen" has been greatly helped by the power of sound. Such as: the mournful sound of singing and playing the Song of the Fishermen; the roar of wild wind and waves, etc. If "Song of the Fishermen" was not dubbed, perhaps the depth of its emotional impact would not have been so great!

The Problem of "Fixed Roles" 301

— Bai Bei

Everyone has the development of their own thoughts. Every actor has their own personality, and this is unchangeable. Of course, an actor can specialize in more than one "specialty," but in the end, it is impossible to find an all-purpose "star"!

But in China, it is not the case. We often see a star playing a "tragic role" in Film A, a "comedic role" in Film B, and a "martial arts character" in Film C. May I ask, how can they have artistic in-depth development if they pursue them without purpose? Is it really like the advertisement says: "All-purpose...?"

Hollywood's Lillian Gish is famous for playing tragedies well. Heifley is famous for his hippie smiles. They are always pursuing what is close to their own character, and they are not comparable to those who are fickle. However, sometimes we can see the wording "changing style" in advertisements. However, it is necessary to recognize that they "change their style" because they find dissatisfaction with their original strengths. Or feel the difficulty of "in-depth study," so there is this "change of style," and it is not that they play whatever role they like.

Cathay Opens "City Love Writes About Abnormal Love in Society" 302

— Ying

Love is originally very sacred; but now in the city, there are often a group of young men and women who regard love as a kind of commodity like a transaction. There are even many people who think that marriage is the tomb of love, and practice the heresy of men and women loving each other without getting married. This is very regrettable. The film "City Love" (Sally Bishop), which is opening at Cathay today, is based on the famous work of the famous novelist Temple Thurstun. It aims to expose the secrets of this abnormal love. The whole film is full of ironic tones, humorous flavors, humorous performances, and passionate emotions. The heroine, Joan Blondell, is not only beautiful in appearance, but also has very considerable subtlety in her expressions. The other male and female supporting roles are also competent.

Film Novel

Film Novel Twentieth Century (6) 303

— Wen Yin

Lilian slipped out of George's arms and walked to the mirror opposite. She suddenly jumped up again and shouted, "That guy hid my makeup box again!" She stood in front of that mirror for a long time. She felt that she was really beautiful, with her eyelids half-closed and her mouth slightly open, showing a shy and innocent look, just like a bride who had not yet married, being helped to the altar. She felt that this expression was too good and should not be wasted. She turned around and shyly said to George, "George, why haven't you ever proposed to me?" George felt strange and said, "I never thought you would be interested in that." Lilian sighed and said: Alas, George, you really know too little about the real Lilian Garland! I only know that she is an actress, but I am tired of the theater. I am not living. I am performing... I am afraid that when I am about to die, I still won't believe that I am really dead. Oh, I have died countless times and fallen in love countless times. I can't tell what is real and what is fake." George walked up to her and asked her in a low voice, "What do you say is real after all?" Lilian blinked her eyes and wiped away her tears, and then said very solemnly, "A house, a home, a small children's room upstairs, with a few cookie jars inside, and the sound of children's feet going up and down the stairs..."

Just as Lilian was saying that, she heard the door behind her open. Her heart beat wildly, and even her breathing was about to stop, because when she turned around, she saw Oscar Jaffe standing at the door, staggering forward. His hand was supported by a wooden frame, which he had thought of at the last minute, and he admired his own cleverness for it. No woman, especially not Lilian, he thought, could see his injured and suffering expression without feeling pity. But he still couldn't put on a sad face, because he had encountered a surprising adventure... that adventure was enough to make him cheer. First, two bearded men came to Jaffe's box to find him. They were important members of a "Passion Play Troupe." They had also escaped because of their failure in Poet's Valley. When they saw Jaffe, they told him about their experiences. Jaffe got an inspiration from this... he could perform the "Passion Play" and have Lilian play the role of Medeline in the play! What's more, a millionaire, Mr. Clark, a deeply religious industrialist, volunteered to help financially. The millionaire said that he would spare no expense to help, and he gave him a large check, saying that it was only the first check!

Jaffe knew Lilian's temper very well. He did not dare to reveal so much good news on his face. All he had on his face were some traces of pain that he was trying to hide. He spoke. He said, "Lilian, I came to see you and say 'Hello'." His voice was extremely soft. But Lilian's voice was very tense. She said, "Oscar, I don't want to talk to you. Please go! I have nothing to say to you! I have no time to listen to anything you have to say"! George heard this and stood up. He scolded Jaffe, "I warn you. Be careful. Don't come here to mess with Miss Garland. What I say is what I say. Get out!" Jaffe was both frightened and ashamed. He said to Lilian, "Lilian, you can ask him to throw me out. This is really an unbelievable thing. My coming here is still magnanimous, regardless of the past... specially to congratulate you on your success." (To be continued)
